- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438577/][MIPS Technologies Launches New Developer Community]]: MIPS launched developer.mips.com community site — targets Android on MIPS, provides Linux kernel source, NDK, development tools, forums; aims to compete with ARM in mobile/embedded space.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/439472/][DISCONTIGMEM, !NUMA, and SLUB]]: Bug where DISCONTIGMEM causes SLUB allocator crashes on non-NUMA systems — DISCONTIGMEM maps memory regions to fake NUMA nodes confusing SLUB; discussion on fixing without breaking embedded systems; problem involves complex tradeoffs between memory models and allocator assumptions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/439314/][Rationalizing the ARM tree]]: Russell King and Linus Torvalds criticized ARM architecture code growth — 75% of arch-specific changes in linux-next are ARM, ~6000 new lines; Linus threatened to not pull ARM tree unless cleanup happens; solution is to consolidate duplicated drivers (GPIO, interrupt chips, clocksource) and use Device Tree to reduce mach/* directories.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/439419/][Managing source code with Mercurial (developerWorks)]]: IBM developerWorks introduction to Mercurial DVCS — triggered debate on Mercurial vs Git; Mercurial has simpler default commands but requires extensions for advanced features; Git has local branches and more powerful rebasing; discussion on branch semantics differences between the two systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437929/][LFCS: Linux penetration, Yocto, and hardware success stories]]: Jim Zemlin's Linux Foundation Collaboration Summit keynote — 95% of top500 supercomputers run Linux, 72% equity trading; Yocto 1.0 released for embedded distro building; hardware panel with TI/Qualcomm/Intel on upstreaming drivers; embedded Linux talent acquisition increasing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438182/][The native KVM tool]]: Pekka Enberg's lightweight KVM management tool as QEMU alternative — minimal features (serial console, no graphics/networking/SMP), clean compact code, easier debugging; being extended with virtio networking and SMP support.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437981/][A JIT for packet filters]]: Eric Dumazet's BPF JIT compiler for 64-bit x86 — translates BPF bytecode to native x86 instructions, 50ns savings per filter invocation; BPF is used by tcpdump and socket filters; potential future application to nftables for firewall rule JIT compilation.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438256/][Explicit block device plugging]]: Jens Axboe's 2.6.39 kernel rewrite of block device plugging — replaced per-device state with per-task blk_plug structure allowing multiple related I/O requests to be batched before dispatch, reducing lock contention and improving request merging for better disk throughput.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438155/][LFCS: ARM, control groups, and the next 20 years]]: Linux Foundation Collaboration Summit kernel panel covering ARM community fragmentation (500+ SoCs, 70 sub-architectures), control groups code quality concerns, Linaro collaboration efforts, and speculation on Linux in 2031 — Gleixner predicted PREEMPT_RT merge before retirement.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437602/][systemd for Administrators, Part VI]]: Lennart Poettering's systemd series part 6 — explains chroot() environment handling in systemd where daemons run in clean, independent contexts without inheriting user shell environment variables unlike sysvinit-based systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/438169/][Poettering: systemd for Administrators, Part VII]]: systemd-analyze blame and plot tools for boot time analysis — emphasizes filing bugs at the right subsystem rather than just blaming slow boot services.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437142/][Kernel release status]]: 2.6.39-rc2 status and stable kernel updates — Linus noted uncommonly calm -rc2 release, suspicious of quiet development period.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/436871/][Linux Filesystem, Storage, and Memory Management Summit, Day 1]]: 2011 summit coverage — writeback problems and direct reclaim elimination discussed (Jan Kara's simpler patch vs Fengguang's bandwidth-based approach), VFS scalability patches status, transcendent memory/zcache updates, memory control group usage by Google/Fujitsu/Red Hat/Parallels/Taobao, memory compaction status, NVM Express standard introduction.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/437066/][Linux Filesystem, Storage, and Memory Management Summit, Day 2]]: Second day coverage — I/O bandwidth controllers (throttling vs proportional), working set estimation for job placement, VM memory sizing with balloon drivers and page hinting, dirty limits in control groups, transparent huge page improvements, NUMA home node proposal, stable pages for writes-in-flight, 9p filesystem improvements for virtualization.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/436041/][Jump label reworked]]: Jump label API rework for 2.6.40 — simplified interface using struct jump_label_key with jump_label_inc/dec and static_branch; enables runtime toggle of unlikely code paths with minimal overhead when jump label support is configured.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/436047/][Powering down APM]]: Len Brown's proposal to remove APM power management support in 2.6.40 — APM obsolete since 2006 (no hardware or Windows support), but removal concerns raised for legacy systems; possibly keep power-off functionality while removing idle support.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/435894/][Dynamic devices and static configuration]]: PandaBoard USB-Ethernet interface naming (usb0 vs eth0) and MAC address problems — discussion of platform_data expansion vs device tree approach for non-discoverable embedded hardware; short-term patches provided while longer-term solutions debated.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/435917/][Fighting fork bombs]]: Hiroyuki Kamezawa's fork bomb tracking and killing mechanism — adds persistent process tree tracking to identify entire process families even after parent exit, detects fork bombs via memory allocation stalls, depth-first traversal to find and kill all descendants of high-memory processes when OOM fires.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/434763/][Report from the V4L2 Warsaw Brainstorming Meeting]]: Three-day brainstorming session covering compressed video format APIs for MPEG/H.264, subdev hierarchy and pool improvements, cropping/composing ioctls, HDMI/CEC rework, buffer pool infrastructure for Linaro, multiple buffer queues, sensor/flash/snapshot functionality.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/435022/][Converting strings to integers]]: New kstrto*() functions for 2.6.39 — standardized string-to-integer converters (kstrtoull, kstrtol, kstrtoint, etc.) marked __must_check to replace old problematic functions like simple_strtoul().
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/434833/][The dynamic debugging interface]]: dynamic_debug kernel feature explanation — pr_debug()/dev_dbg() calls controlled via /sys/kernel/debug/dynamic_debug/control using selectors (file, function, module, format) and flags (+p, -p, f/l/m/t) for runtime debug output control.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/434821/][Persistent storage for a kernel's "dying breath"]]: Tony Luck and Thomas Gleixner's pstore filesystem for 2.6.39 — generic framework for saving crash information to platform-specific persistent storage (ACPI ERST, flash, etc.) across reboots, mounted at /dev/pstore.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/434901/][R Cookbook]]: O'Reilly cookbook by Paul Teetor for R statistical programming — 200+ recipes covering data structures, statistics, graphics, linear regression, practical data analysis.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/435064/][O'Reilly Media and Fluidinfo Contest]]: O'Reilly and Fluidinfo API contest for developers to create applications using O'Reilly book metadata in Fluidinfo's writable API.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433787/][Diving into the Linux Networking Stack, Part I]]: Michael Schultz's tutorial on Linux networking stack — driver initialization and packet reception flow through igb driver example.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433904/][A group scheduling demonstration]]: Jonathan Corbet's demonstration of per-session group scheduling in 2.6.38 — runaway GUI processes isolated to their own cgroup, desktop remained responsive despite heavy load.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433568/][Uprobes: 11th time is the charm?]]: Uprobes dynamic user-space probing update — execute-out-of-line mechanism for breakpoint insertion, ftrace integration, SystemTap interest but gdb suitability questioned; controversial XOL VMA injection approach.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433601/][APIs for sensors]]: Sensor subsystem API discussion — pressure sensor driver rejected from input subsystem (not human input), IIO subsystem for analog-to-digital converters, debate over hwmon vs miscdevice vs IIO location.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433107/][Kuhn: GPL Compliance of Red Hat Linux Distribution]]: Bradley Kuhn's analysis of RHEL GPL compliance — Red Hat's changelog in src.rpm satisfies letter of GPLv2§2(a) but criticized for obfuscating kernel changes; community debate on "preferred form for modifications".
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433561/][Qt and Digia, facts and fiction]]: Qt Blog clarification after Nokia-Digia deal — 400K developers, 3500 commercial customers, Nokia continues investing in Qt, LGPL licensing maintained, KDE Free Qt Foundation guarantees BSD-style license if FLOSS releases cease.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/432871/][HP: The Linux Desktop Company]]: ZDNet coverage of HP shipping WebOS devices — HP's strategy to avoid Windows license costs, WebOS on tablets/notebooks/printers/phones, discussion of Linux desktop adoption.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/433637/][LPI Hosts Exam Labs in Poland and Greece]]: Linux Professional Institute certification exam labs at 4Developers conference in Warsaw and Thessaloniki.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/427048/][Linus Torvalds interview]]: ITWire interview covering Linux evolution, mobile phones (Nokia mentioned), community growth vs early hacker days, technical challenge remains fun.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/427104/][Increasing the TCP initial congestion window]]: Google's patch to increase TCP initial congestion window from 4 to 10 segments — 10% latency reduction in tests, also raises initial receive window to 10 segments in 2.6.38.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426961/][Removing ext2 and/or ext3]]: Jan Kara's proposal to drop ext2/ext3 codebase — ext4 can mount ext2/3 with compatibility and optimizations like delayed allocation, but compatibility modes less tested; concerns about ext2 bitrot and testing gaps for non-native ext4 modes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426921/][Supporting multiple LSMs]]: David Howells' multi-LSM stacking framework patches — allows multiple security modules to register and be called for access decisions; Glass LSM alternative from Casey Schaufler uses different composition approach; secid handling problematic for SELinux+Smack combination.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426947/][Mesh networking with batman-adv]]: BATMAN-adv mesh networking merged into 2.6.38 — works at link layer via virtual network device, broadcasts originator messages for routing discovery, scales to ~1000 nodes; limited security against spoofed OGMs; useful for building/neighborhood connectivity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426912/][FOSDEM: Collaboration between distributions]]: FOSDEM 2011 distribution track — Debian/Fedora/openSUSE collaboration manifesto, downstream packaging cooperation, Mageia fork from Mandriva, Gentoo governance reform.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/426451/][Distribution quotes of the week]]: Linux community quotes — Debian on BeagleBoards, Joe Brockmeier on openSUSE release schedules.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478627/][Format string vulnerabilities]]: Jake Edge's detailed explanation of format string vulnerabilities using the sudo bug as example — user-controlled argv[0] passed as format string to vfprintf(), allowing privilege escalation via %n format specifier to overwrite UID; fix is using %s in final print statement.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478139/][Format string vulnerability in sudo]]: Brief note that sudo 1.8.0-1.8.3p1 has a format string vulnerability in sudo_debug() that can crash or potentially escalate privileges; fixed in 1.8.3p2; -D_FORTIFY_SOURCE=2 helps block exploits.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478635/][KaKaRoTo: How the ECDSA algorithm works]]: Youness Alaoui explains elliptic curve digital signature algorithm math — Sony's PS3 used weak ECDSA implementation with predictable random numbers, allowing private key extraction; fixed in firmware 3.56 with new keys.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478440/][What happened to disk performance in 2.6.39]]: Jonathan Corbet investigates SSD performance drop in 2.6.39 — explicit plugging/unplugging in generic_file_aio_read() caused readahead I/O to stall; fix removes top-level plugging so readahead requests bypass the plug and reach hardware immediately.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/478111/][Preparing for user-space checkpoint/restore]]: Covers CRIU (kernel patches for process checkpoint/restore via prctl, /proc extensions, kcmp() syscall) and DMTCP (pure user-space solution using LD_PRELOAD wrappers, supports MPI, no kernel changes needed).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/496418/][Who owns your data?]]: Jake Edge discusses digital heritage and data preservation — argues open formats trump proprietary/DRM-locked formats; free software supports old formats longer than vendors; Internet Archive can only preserve so much; users should demand open standards from businesses and governments.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/496583/][TizenConf: Pitching HTML5 as a development framework]]: Nathan Willis covers Tizen Developer Conference — HTML5/Web API as primary dev platform, Smack-based security, ConnMan 1.0 with fast DHCP, W3C Core Mobile Web Platform Group participation, Facebook's RingMark compliance test tool; small community but "code leads" strategy.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/496158/][Accounting systems: a rant and a quest]]: Jonathan Corbet recounts LWN's QuickBooks hitting hidden 14,500 item limit forcing $2400 enterprise upgrade — impetus to finally migrate to free software accounting; surveys landscape: GnuCash/KMyMoney too basic, enterprise tools too complex; ledger-style plain-text approach discussed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/496099/][Internet censorship and OONI]]: Jake Edge covers Tor's OONI project for detecting network interference — crowdsourced censorship measurement via ooni-probe framework; found blocked Palestinian news sites and T-Mobile WebGuard overblocking; open methodology vs Google's closed Transparency Report.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/495987/][Linux Format censored over 'Learn to Hack' feature (bit-tech)]]: Brief note that Barnes & Noble pulled Linux Format issue 154 over "Learn to Hack" Metasploit cover feature; TuxRADAR published article online; debate on "hacker" vs "cracker" terminology and private retailer censorship rights.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494463/][Quantum random numbers]]: Jake Edge covers ANU's Quantum Random Number Generator — 5.7 Gbit/s from quantum vacuum fluctuations, fastest RNG in world; hardware RNGs overrated: 256 bits of entropy sufficient for cryptography when fed through cryptographic PRNG (AES can do 713 MB/s); no HTTPS yet means man-in-the-middle could intercept; Lua used in entropy daemon.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494035/][Android trojan steals keystrokes using phone movements (ars technica)]]: TapLogger proof-of-concept app uses accelerometer/gyroscope/orientation sensors to infer keystrokes; fix proposals: disable sensors during sensitive input, split permissions for background sensor access, randomized keypad layouts; discussion on capability-based security model.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/493533/][An Interview With Linus Torvalds (TechCrunch)]]: TechCrunch interview covering quiet computers, desktop building, Linux advocacy; Linus prefers silent workstations; community discussion on fanless PCs, mini-ITX builds, Antec P180/P280 cases, ThinkPad thinkfan control, water cooling, SSD-only systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494388/][git.kernel.org mirror at Google]]: Google now mirrors kernel.org at kernel.googlesource.com — uses JGit with BigTable storage, smart HTTP protocol only, no rsync; mirror polls git:// every 30 min for consistency; SSL latency ~400ms, modified Git protocol helper to reuse SSL connections planned for git.git's contrib/.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494028/][O_HOT and O_COLD]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Ted Ts'o's proposal for O_HOT/O_COLD file creation flags to hint filesystem about data access frequency; ext4 implements by placing hot files in low-numbered blocks; criticism: unclear semantics, 'hotness' varies within files, different policies per filesystem, should let OS observe access patterns vs developers guessing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494158/][Toward a safer fput()]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Al Viro's fput() locking solution — rename old fput() to fput_nodefer(), new fput() defers work asynchronously via task_work_add(); IMA appraisal extension deadlock problem; task_work_add() runs work before returning to user space ensuring close() semantics preserved; ~6 architectures need patches for task_work_add().
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494252/][A library for seccomp filters]]: Jake Edge covers libseccomp by Paul Moore — API for BPF-based seccomp mode 2; seccomp_init(), seccomp_rule_add(), seccomp_load(), seccomp_release(); actions: SCMP_ACT_KILL, SCMP_ACT_TRAP, SCMP_ACT_ERRNO, SCMP_ACT_TRACE; arg filtering with SCMP_A0-SCMP_A5 macros; LGPLv2.1 license; used by vsftpd 3.0.0 and Chromium.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/493411/][An Alternative Reading of the IADB Study on Peru's OLPC Implementation (OLPC News)]]: Oscar Becerra (former Peruvian Ministry of Education) responds to Economist criticism — OLPC primary goal was improving children's lives via 21st century tools, not test scores; Table 5 shows dramatic increase in computer access/use; Table 7 shows better cognitive skills; better tools for future vs immediate test improvement.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494265/][Android Cookbook--New from O'Reilly Media]]: New O'Reilly book by Ian Darwin — 200+ recipes crowdsourced from AndroidCookbook.com; covers UI controls, multitouch, layouts, multimedia, camera, GPS, web services; BlackBerry now accepts Android apps; worked example-driven approach for experienced Java developers moving to Android.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494500/][FreeBSD Device Drivers--New from No Starch Press]]: New No Starch Press book by Joseph Kong (author of Designing BSD Rootkits) — guide to FreeBSD driver development; covers Newbus framework, ISA/PCI/USB buses, DMA, interrupt handling; practical chapters on parallel port, USB printer, Intel Gigabit Ethernet drivers; CAM for HBAs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494502/][Using Drupal, 2nd Edition--New from O'Reilly Media]]: New O'Reilly book on Drupal 7 by Angela Byron, Addison Berry, Bruno De Bondt — project-based chapters with step-by-step recipes; covers Drupal concepts, building blocks, configuration; new modules including Drupal Commerce, Media, Workbench; aimed at beginners through experienced developers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494499/][LoMus 2012]]: Fourth edition of libre music software competition — search for open-source software for musical/intermedia creation; submission deadline April 29; awards ceremony May 11 at JIM 2012; prizes for innovative open-source audio/music software.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494497/][CloudOpen from the Linux Foundation]]: New Linux Foundation conference co-located with LinuxCon in San Diego August 2012 — covers Chef, Gluster, Hadoop, KVM, Linux, oVirt, Puppet, Xen; big data strategies, open cloud platforms; CFP open until June 1.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/494491/][Wendy Seltzer to Keynote Ohio LinuxFest 2012]]: Wendy Seltzer (W3C Policy Counsel, Harvard Berkman Fellow) to keynote Ohio LinuxFest September 2012 — founded Chilling Effects Clearinghouse; board of Tor Project; works on copyright, trademark, patent, open source, privacy issues.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492859/][LFCS 2012: The Linux System Definition]]: Jake Edge covers OIN CEO Keith Bergelt at Linux Foundation Collaboration Summit — OIN patents now cover 1800 packages (expanded from 1100); 440+ licensees; defensive publications against bad patents; Google/IBM/OIN Code Search for prior art; Microsoft using 25 patents to attack mobile Linux; Tizen/webOS/MeeGo add resilience.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492624/][LFCS 2012: The future of GLIBC]]: Jake Edge covers Carlos O'Donell and Roland McGrath at LFCS — GLIBC moving to consensus-driven self-governance; dissolved steering committee; libc-alpha moderation removed; 25-30 committers; C11 atomic operations coming in 2.16; libm almost complete; TIRPC split; EGLIBC merger discussions; testing framework needs work; long-term: tracing support, auto-generated libm, exception-less syscalls.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492959/][Allocating uninitialized file blocks]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Zheng Liu's FALLOC_FL_NO_HIDE_STALE flag for fallocate() — marks blocks as initialized without writing zeros; benchmark: 76s to 18s for random-write workload; security concerns (sysctl default off, CAP_SYS_RAWIO); Ric Wheeler calls it security hole; alternative: background scrubber process; ext4 vs XFS performance comparison.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492125/][Toward more reliable logging]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Kay Sievers' structured printk() patch — record-oriented log buffer with sequence numbers; printk_emit() for dictionary KEY=value pairs; /dev/kmsg now supports read/poll; format: priority,seq,time;message\nSUBSYSTEM=...\nDEVICE=...; Linus suggested splitting record format for 3.4 merge; discussion on lumberjack/CEE/JSON structured logging standards.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492296/][LTTng 2.0: Tracing for power users and developers - part 2]]: Mathieu Desnoyers et al. — combined kernel/user-space tracing with lttng-ust; performance counter calibration with kretprobes; LTTngTop ncurses tool for trace analysis; flight recorder snapshots; live trace streaming in development; use cases: interrupt handler timing, fsync bottlenecks, distributed filesystem cache sizing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/493164/][(deferred) bits from the DPL: March 2012]]: Stefano Zacchiroli's Debian Project Leader report — 5-year hardware replacement plan (9k/year); Debian accepted for Google Summer of Code; DEP-5 (debian/copyright format) ACCEPTED; trademark guidelines for encumbered software; DuckDuckGo revenue sharing; .debian.net domains opened; Debian 7 (Wheezy) freeze upcoming.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492624/][LFCS 2012: The future of GLIBC]]: Jake Edge covers Carlos O'Donell and Roland McGrath at LFCS — GLIBC moving to consensus-driven self-governance; dissolved steering committee; libc-alpha moderation removed; 25-30 committers; C11 atomic operations coming in 2.16; libm almost complete; TIRPC split; EGLIBC merger discussions; testing framework needs work; long-term: tracing support, auto-generated libm, exception-less syscalls.

DEVICE=...; Linus suggested splitting record format for 3.4 merge; discussion on lumberjack/CEE/JSON structured logging standards.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492138/][Langley: False Start's Failure]]: Jake Edge covers Adam Langley explaining why Google ended its False Start SSL experiment — hardware SSL terminators caused issues; scheme required internet-wide scanning to build blacklist of problematic sites; Google ending support after list erosion; False Start still works with SPDY servers using NPN; discussion of SSL warnings, certificate verification, self-signed certs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492885/][The H Speed Guide to Lua]]: ris covers The H's Lua programming language guide — 20k lines of ANSI C, 182KB memory footprint; register-based VM with bytecode; incremental garbage collection; designed for embedding; LuaJIT2 supports x86, x86-64, ARM, PPC, MIPS; coroutines from C unparalleled; debate on 1-based arrays, indentation syntax vs braces, lack of regex vs patterns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492714/][PHP: a fractal of bad design]]: Jake Edge covers Eevee's detailed criticism of PHP — 'virtually every feature is broken'; predictability, consistency, reliability, debuggability, security issues; comparison to BASIC's mental mutilation; extensive discussion on language design, competence, C vs Perl predictability, sequence points, undefined behavior.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/492955/][Head First C]]: O'Reilly Media press release for new C programming book by David Griffiths — brain-friendly guide covering language basics, pointers, dynamic memory, multi-threading, network programming; C as entry point to understanding computers; suitable as college textbook.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491555/][Bug reports: information or spam?]]: Nathan Willis covers Debian bug tracking debate — Welle's bug rejected for blacklisted URL (foo.org on uribl); RFC 2606 example domains suggested; spam filters vs user experience; Debian BTS email-only reporting limitations; reportbug tool; discussion on SMTP blocking, HTTP fallback, air-gapped networks.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491258/][LFCS 2012: The kernel panel]]: Jake Edge covers kernel panel at LFCS — Greg KH moderating; panelists: Mel Gorman (memory management), John Linville (wireless), James Bottomley (SCSI), Keith Packard (graphics); topics: NUMA migration schemes, containers/cgroups, 802.11ac, X vs Wayland, stable kernel releases, structured logging, SCSI future, bufferbloat, Android patches, power measurement, hardware bypass.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491440/][SELinuxDenyPtrace and security by default]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Fedora 17's SELinuxDenyPtrace feature — ptrace() allows any program to inspect other processes owned by same user; feature denies ptrace by default; broke gdb, strace, DrKonqi; debate over security vs convenience; Ubuntu uses Yama module; discussion on user vs program privileges, Android's per-app UID model, capabilities for binaries.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491516/][Remote root hole in Samba]]: Samba security releases 3.6.4, 3.5.14, 3.4.16 fix CVE-2012-1182 — PIDL-based autogenerated code allowed overwriting beyond allocated array; remote code execution as root; bug in IDL compiler; existed since ~2007; discussion on managed languages vs C, bounds checking, fat pointers, chroot jails.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490855/][AT&T Microcell FAIL]]: FailOverflow analysis of AT&T 3G femtocell — runs Busybox/Linux; hardcoded backdoor called 'BackdoorPacketCmdLine'; UDP packets execute commands via backticksh; port globally accessible; encouraged placed behind NAT; UPnP hole punching concerns; 3G femtocells generally rootable; GPL questions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490973/][Wheeler: Insecure open source software libraries?]]: David Wheeler blog post — bundled libraries lose security advantage of OSS since fixes aren't used; developers don't update embedded libs; distributions ship old versions; Google Chromium bundles; discussion on library stability, API compatibility, distribution patching, games bundling SDL/ogg.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491716/][A new security subsystem wiki]]: Kernel.org wiki down after breakin; kernel security developers created kernsec.org wiki; also btrfs wiki moved to btrfs.ipv5.de; discussion of redirecting old wiki.kernel.org addresses.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491722/][SCHED_DEADLINE returns]]: Jonathan Corbet covers deadline scheduling patches — processes declare max CPU time and deadline; scheduler ensures deadlines met; new developer Juri Lelli maintaining; git repo, test app, mailing list; WCET (worst-case execution time) hard to determine; priority inheritance patches still need work.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491310/][A new approach to user namespaces]]: Jonathan Corbet covers Eric Biederman's user namespace patches — kuid_t/kgid_t types to separate kernel IDs from namespace IDs; prevents mixing errors; make_kuid(), from_kuid(), from_kuid_munged() functions; uid_map setup via /proc; container root can set up sub-namespaces; CAP_SETUID privilege; makes containers more secure.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491653/][Finding the right evolutionary niche]]: Neil Brown on Android's 'timed gpio' driver for vibrators — Android added separate driver vs modifying existing; examined gpio, leds, input subsystems; input force-feedback framework provides 'rumble' with fail-safe timer; reassigning vibrator functionality; highlights need for persistence when finding right kernel niche.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491510/][LTTng 2.0: Tracing for power users and developers - part 1]]: Mathieu Desnoyers et al. introduce LTTng 2.0 tracer — rewrite of 0.x; works on vanilla kernels 2.6.38+; combined kernel and user-space tracing; CTF (Common Trace Format); multi-user, multiple sessions; Babeltrace converter; comparison with Perf and Ftrace; installation on Ubuntu 12.04.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491237/][The state of Wayland]]: Brief summary of Wayland status — GTK+ 3.4.1 and Qt5 have complete Wayland support except CSD; EFL and Clutter complete support; applications need toolkit support not Xlib; discussion on remote Wayland (vncserver), xpra, SPICE, input redirection, window management API.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491075/][A report from the Peru OLPC deployment]]: Economist summary of IDB report on Peru OLPC — no improvement in math/reading; positive impacts on computer skills; cognitive abilities from programs aimed at thinking processes; high-quality instruction still needed; discussion on Khan Academy, Sugata Mitra's Hole in the Wall, Uruguay/Paraguay success vs Peru failures.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491515/][Linux for Your Electric Car]]: Tumanako Project — open source EV drive package and inverter for 200kW induction motor; 6 months to full open source; SPICE inversion mentioned; developer Philip Court.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/491560/][Build Awesome Command-Line Applications in Ruby]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf press release — David Copeland's book on Ruby CLI apps; self-documenting, robust, adaptable; free open source parsers; defaults for simple use; man pages and help; testing CLI apps.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490457/][Why bother supporting ARM?]]: Jonathan Corbet on Fedora ARM as primary architecture — ARM messy with many vendors; lack of hardware discoverability; no binary blobs policy; device tree consolidation; ARM slower for builds; ARM dominant in mobile Linux; Fedora criteria for architecture promotion; disruptive technology dilemma for Red Hat.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490516/][An update on Oracle v. Google]]: Adam Saunders covers Oracle vs Google trial (April 16) — Java copyright/patent infringement; Google used clean room implementation; most Oracle patents rejected via reexamination; only '104 (JIT) and '520 (static init) remain; API copyright claim weak (Baker v. Selden); Android code no longer in Android; FSF argues GPL Java should have been used; Android under threat from Apple, Microsoft patents too.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490291/][Runtime filesystem consistency checking]]: Jake Edge covers 'Recon' system from University of Toronto — runtime consistency checking instead of offline fsck; global invariants transformed to local; ext3 has 33 invariants checked at transaction commit; sits between filesystem and block layer; caught errors fsck missed; 2% I/O overhead; performance impact modest; comparison to lockdep.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490518/][Libsecret revealed]]: Nathan Willis covers Stef Walter's libsecret library — replaces libgnome-keyring; thread-safe, introspectable, async; full Secret Service API over D-Bus; works with GNOME and KDE secret services; simple password API + complete API; Python/JavaScript examples; migration for GNOME 3.6.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490394/][OSADL on realtime Linux determinism]]: OSADL press release — year of latency testing on PREEMPT_RT kernels; 730+ latency plots per system; AMD Athlon, ARM OMAP, MIPS Loongson, Intel Atom, VIA C7 tested; absence of outliers demonstrates generic deterministic behavior; 100 µs vs 50 µs differences across kernel versions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/490413/][Udev and systemd to merge]]: Kay Sievers announces udev merging into systemd — udev 45 jumps to systemd 184; built from same source tree; separate binaries (udevd, systemd); compatible with non-systemd init; libudev API untouched; reduces code duplication; separate builds for outside-systemd (initrd support); discussion on feature bloat, Zawinski's Law.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/489480/][Grinberg: Linux on an 8-bit micro?]]: Dmitry Grinberg wrote ARM emulator for ATmega1284p — 2 hours to boot to bash, 4 more for full Ubuntu; effective speed 6.5KHz; SD card formatting possible; hand-soldered board; extreme example of emulation overhead; discussion on earliest Unix machines, Minix, ELKS, Z80 UZI.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/520227/][Al Viro's new execve/kernel_thread design]]: Detailed technical explanation of new kernel thread creation design; replaces convoluted old kernel_thread() implementation; clean approach across multiple architectures (alpha, x86, um, arm, mips, c6x); kernel_execve() now completely generic; per-architecture conversion independent.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/520012/][EPOLL_CTL_DISABLE and multithreaded applications]]: Michael Kerrisk; new epoll operation solves race conditions deleting file descriptors in multithreaded apps; requires EPOLLONESHOT flag; user-space cache coordination; Paton Lewis patch merged in 3.7; better design could have avoided bolt-on hack.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/520076/][Software interrupts and realtime]]: Jonathan Corbet; Linux softirq mechanism explained; 3.6.1-rt1 realtime patch changes softirq handling to tie processing to threads that generate them; reduces latency and nondeterministic behavior; ksoftirqd exception for hardware interrupt context; potential for eventual softirq elimination.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518955/][CIA.vc shuts down]]: Joey Hess; centralized commit notification service shutdown September 2012; no backups; replacement options irker (decentralized JSON relay) and KGB (Debian project, SOAP API); Eric Raymond designed irker before shutdown; decentralized approach now favored over centralized CIA model.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/519010/][Loading modules from file descriptors]]: Michael Kerrisk; Kees Cook finit_module() syscall for Chrome OS; allows loading modules directly from fd without copying to buffer; enables origin verification via filesystem trust; LSM integration for signature checking via extended attributes; merged in Linux 3.8 with flags argument.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/519244/][The Linux Foundation's UEFI secure boot system]]: James Bottomley pre-bootloader proposal; Microsoft signed first-stage; present user test keystrokes required; chain loads unsigned bootloader; vs Shim/MOK approach; Matthew Garrett criticism of user intervention friction; enables booting unsigned code on secure boot systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518705/][The CryptoParty Handbook]]: 390-page privacy guide published October 2012; created collaboratively in 3 days at Studio Weise7 Berlin; CC-BY-SA 4.0 license; covers operational security, encryption tools, network privacy; still evolving; contributors welcome.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518717/][Samsung's F2FS filesystem]]: Flash-Friendly FileSystem for NAND flash memory; log-structured approach adapted for eMMC/SD card FTL; handles snowball effect write amplification; Samsung designed for their own flash devices; Arnd Bergmann classification of FTL types (remapping vs log-structured); merged in Linux 3.8.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518953/][The new visibility of RCU processing]]: Paul McKenney; Linux 3.6+ moved RCU grace-period handling from softirq to kthreads (rcu_sched/rcu_preempt/rcu_bh); improves real-time latency on large systems by allowing preemption; overhead unchanged, just more visible; per-grace-period ~30 microseconds; can handle 100+ updates per grace period; ~300ns per-update overhead.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518988/][An f2fs teardown]]: Neil Brown technical analysis of F2FS internals; 4K blocks, 2MB segments, sections grouped into zones; 6 open sections for hot/warm/cold data separation; copy-on-write with FTL cooperation; NAT (Node Address Table) for indirect node addressing; no snapshots due to dual-location metadata; directory uses hashed buckets with stable telldir addresses; max 16TB filesystem 4TB files.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/519085/][getauxval() and the auxiliary vector]]: Michael Kerrisk; glibc 2.16 added getauxval() function to retrieve kernel-supplied auxiliary vector values; communicates AT_PHDR AT_ENTRY AT_HWCAP AT_SYSINFO_EHDR etc; used by dynamic linker; AT_RANDOM provides 16 random bytes for stack canary; AT_SECURE flags setuid/setgid execution; eliminates need for direct /proc/self/auxv parsing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/519020/][HTTPS Everywhere 3.0]]: EFF released version 3.0 of HTTPS Everywhere Firefox extension; now encrypts 1500+ websites; estimate of 100 billion page views and trillions of HTTP requests encrypted annually; double the coverage of previous releases.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/519045/][Practical Vim]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book by Drew Neil; 100+ Vim tips; covers Dot Formula, macros, jumplist, spell-checker, regexp; without plugins; companion to vimcasts.org tutorials.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518232/][XDC2012: Programming languages for X application development]]: Bart Massey at X.Org Developers Conference; argues desktop apps harder than mobile/web due to C/C++ pain points; suggests Java or Python instead; mobile/web use memory-managed languages; C/C++ toolkits (GTK/Qt) amplify complexity; Tcl/Tk praised but considered dated; concluded "if we're going to save the desktop, programming language is part of the problem."
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518265/][LSS: Security modules and RPM]]: Elena Reshetova at Linux Security Summit 2012; proposed generalized security plugin hooks for RPM to support multiple LSMs (SELinux, Smack); symmetric before/after hooks for transactions and package operations; file-level hooks for labeling/hashing; conflicts hook for per-package decisions; sepolicy RPM plugin as model; would allow non-native installers to use security functionality.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518457/][Standardizing virtio]]: Rusty Russell proposal to OASIS for virtio 1.0 standardization; aims for formal spec to increase visibility/adoption beyond Linux/KVM; use PCI capabilities for infinite feature bits; decouple experimental development from standard; core specification bus-independent with PCI/mmio appendices.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518480/][Questioning link restrictions]]: Linux 3.6 introduced security restrictions on hard/soft links in world-writable directories; single report of breakage caused Linus to question default enablement; concerns about breaking old scripts; Kees Cook argues benefits outweigh pain; may be reversed if more breakage reports emerge.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518345/][Another LSM stacking approach]]: Casey Schaufler proposed LSM composer solution to allow multiple Linux Security Modules simultaneously; works with SELinux/Smack/AppArmor/TOMOYO/Yama combinations; defers SELinux+Smack stacking as "quite a challenge"; calls all LSM hooks for each access decision; uses composer_ops array replacing single security_ops; Yama stacks for free; CONFIG_SECURITY_COMPOSER enables; performance "within noise."
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518281/][CyanogenMod OTA update manager]]: CyanogenMod 10 (Android 4.1 Jelly Bean) gets native OTA update manager; downloads ROM images from get.cm; automatic update checking (previously paid ROM Manager feature); shows only updates for installed version; ROM Manager still available for flexibility.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518417/][Yocto-Compliant Enea Linux 2.0]]: Embedded distribution based on Yocto; LightWeight Runtime Threads (LWRT) technology for improved real-time user-space scheduling; message passing and resource management; minimal overhead for deterministic applications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/518301/][XDC2012: OpenGL futures]]: Ian Romanick presentation on Mesa/OpenGL ABI restructuring; split libGL into libOpenGL and libGLX; deprecate GLX in favor of EGL; make OpenGL ES part of standard ABI; update loader/driver interface; enable mobile developers to use X as test bed; indirect rendering to be dropped.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/517384/][LSS: Kernel security subsystem reports]]: Jake Edge at Linux Security Summit 2012; crypto API new user-space interface for hardware accelerators; AppArmor policy compiler 2-4x faster 30-50% smaller policies; key management logon key type for CIFS; SELinux filename_trans for proper labeling; IMA digital signature support; Smack 255-char labels for mobile; Yama ptrace restrictions Ubuntu/ChromeOS.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/517465/][Adding a huge zero page]]: Jonathan Corbet; transparent huge pages broke zero-page sharing optimization; process with 200MB of zero pages would show only 4KB with small zero page; but with THP enabled allocates full 200MB; Kirill Shutemov patch adds huge zero page (2MB on x86_64); lazy allocation with reference counting; target for 3.8 kernel.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/517475/][Supervisor mode access prevention]]: Jonathan Corbet; Intel SMAP (Supervisor Mode Access Prevention) new feature in Haswell; prevents kernel from accessing user memory while in privileged mode; uses STAC/CLAC instructions; blocks exploits via bad kernel pointers; found bugs in drivers; merged in 3.7; hardware shipped 2013.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/517237/][GCC Compiler Intrinsics for Vector Processing]]: Linux Journal article; GCC intrinsics for vector processing on X86 (MMX/SSE/SSE2), ARM (Neon), Freescale (Altivec); between assembly and C; debugging tips; ORC as alternative; auto-vectorization often preferable; dispatch via IFUNC for runtime CPU selection.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/516334/][LSS: Integrity for directories and special files]]: Dmitry Kasatkin at LSS 2012; IMA/EVM extended to protect directory contents and special files (symlinks, device nodes); hash over directory entry list (name, inode, type, offset); ima_dir_check() hook during path lookup; prevents offline attacks via file renaming/moving/deleting; ima_link_check() for symbolic links and device nodes.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/512487/][The return of power-aware scheduling]]: Alex Shi proposal; sched_mc_power_savings removed in 3.5; power vs performance modes; x86 all CPUs must idle for deep sleep; best power savings = best performance; 100μs threshold for CPU bringup; ARM big.LITTLE complexity; scheduling domains need power parameters.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/512779/][LPI supports Software Freedom Day in Kenya with Linux Essentials]]: LPI and its East Africa affiliate announced support for Software Freedom Day in Kenya, hosting a Linux Essentials exam lab and co-sponsoring an Open Source Developer Challenge at Strathmore University.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/511421/][Making workqueues non-reentrant]]: Tejun Heo's patch series makes all kernel workqueues non-reentrant, simplifying the API and eliminating subtle bugs caused by concurrent execution of the same work item on multiple CPUs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/511105/][Firmware loading and suspend/resume]]: Ming Lei's patch caches firmware blobs during system suspend so they're available at resume time without requiring filesystem access or user-space involvement, making firmware loading more robust.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/511254/][TCP friends]]: Google's "TCP friends" patch accelerates local TCP connections by bypassing the network stack when both endpoints are on the same machine, achieving speeds up to 5x faster than Unix-domain sockets.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/511259/][Signed overflow optimization hazards in the kernel]]: Paul McKenney explains how compilers exploit signed integer overflow undefined behavior to optimize code, potentially causing bugs in the kernel and how to avoid reliance on signed overflow.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/510046/][The Linux digital audio workstation - Part 2]]: Dave Phillips reviews additional Linux DAWs including MusE 2.0, Non DAW, Qtractor, Renoise, Rosegarden, and Traverso, noting Bitwig Studio as an upcoming cross-platform option.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/510373/][Rigo: Multicore Programming in PyPy and CPython]]: PyPy developer Armin Rigo proposes Automatic Mutual Exclusion (AME) as a higher-level approach to multithreaded Python programming without requiring the GIL.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/509438/][Walsh: SELinux Apache Security Study]]: Dan Walsh comments on a study showing SELinux doesn't prevent all Apache vulnerabilities but contains them, explaining that SELinux limits what a compromised Apache process can access.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/509577/][Testing for kernel performance regressions]]: Mel Gorman's MMTests benchmarks reveal various kernel performance regressions on older hardware (Pentium 4, Phenom II) that core developers may not notice due to testing on newer systems.
