- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/595079/][Fedora Present and Future Part III (Fedora Magazine)]]: Matthew Miller continues his Fedora.next update with part 3 covering governance, progress, and ideas for Fedora's future direction.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/594535/][Numerical Python (Linux Journal)]]: The Linux Journal explores NumPy, an N-dimensional array Python extension that provides optimized numerical computing through multidimensional arrays and operator overloading, though performance challenges arise with individual element access.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/593676/][Much ado about debugging]]: Jonathan Corbet describes how a systemd/kernel debug flag interaction spiraled into community drama, but was ultimately resolved through fixes on both sides including rate-limiting for /proc/kmsg and systemd recognizing systemd.debug separately.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/593918/][Sealed files]]: David Herrmann's file sealing patch set for shmfs allows processes to protect shared memory regions from modification using fcntl() seals, with a new memfd_create() system call providing a filesystem-free way to create sealable memory segments.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/593060/][Pyston — a new Python 2.7 implementation]]: Dropbox announced Pyston, a JIT-based Python 2.7 implementation using LLVM with type speculation for optimization, though the project is in early development and has sparked debate over Python 2 vs Python 3 adoption.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/593565/][St. Pierre: Xwayland]]: Jasper St. Pierre describes the Xwayland back end that was merged into the X server core, featuring a complete rearchitecture that makes it leaner, cleaner, and faster, though direct rendering and 2D acceleration are still in development.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592091/][Ideas for supporting shingled magnetic recording (SMR)]]: At the 2014 LSFMM Summit, Dave Chinner and Ted Ts'o discussed supporting SMR devices, with Chinner proposing to split filesystems into namespace and block allocation layers to optimize for different device types.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592093/][Data integrity user-space interfaces]]: Darrick Wong and Zach Brown led a session at the 2014 LSFMM Summit on progress in user-space interfaces for data integrity using DIF/DIX to add CRC protection to blocks between user space and disk.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592094/][Copy offload]]: Martin Petersen and Zach Brown presented on copy offload at the 2014 LSFMM Summit, a mechanism for handling file copies on storage arrays without CPU or network involvement using SCSI XCOPY, with discussion of LID1 and LID4 token-based copying options.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592096/][Error handling]]: Hannes Reinecke led sessions at the 2014 LSFMM Summit on improving block layer error handling, including detailed I/O error codes and a proposal for recovering from SCSI errors with targeted resets at appropriate levels.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592116/][A revoke() update and more]]: Al Viro gave an update on the revoke() system call at the 2014 LSFMM Summit, describing progress toward closing file descriptors for exclusive file access, along with work to unify read()/write() with readv()/writev() and splice variants.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592645/][Thin provisioning]]: At the 2014 LSFMM Summit, Eric Sandeen and others discussed thin provisioning with dm-thin, addressing performance issues with block allocation, filesystem interaction problems with ENOSPC, and discard/TRIM support.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592098/][Block multi-queue status]]: Nic Bellinger presented on block layer multi-queue at the 2014 LSFMM Summit, reporting that initial work was merged in 3.13 with virtio_block, and describing prototype SCSI conversion achieving 1.7 million IOPS though issues remain with tags and submission models.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592101/][Large-sector drives]]: Ric Wheeler led a session at the 2014 LSFMM Summit on supporting large-sector drives (>4K), noting that storage arrays use 64K and 128K sectors internally and discussing the challenges with page-sized I/O assumptions throughout the kernel.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592102/][Direct I/O status]]: Kent Overstreet presented on his rewrite of direct I/O code at the 2014 LSFMM Summit, leveraging the immutable biovec work to simplify DIO by allocating bios with page batches, reducing code size and complexity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591780/][Facebook and the kernel]]: Chris Mason presented at the 2014 LSFMM Summit on how Facebook uses the Linux kernel, sharing infrastructure statistics and pain points including stable pages, CFQ scheduler, buffered I/O latency, and fine-grained I/O priorities.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592070/][The S-CRIB password scrambler]]: Smart Crib's S-CRIB Scrambler is a 0 USB HSM that computes SHA1-HMAC for password verification, providing irretrievable password storage but raising questions about throughput, SHA1 security, and hardware failure recovery.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591690/][Various page cache issues]]: At the 2014 LSFMM Summit, developers discussed page cache issues including 32-bit system limitations with large drives, larger pages in the page cache, and removing filesystem block mappings from the page cache.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591782/][Support for shingled magnetic recording devices]]: Martin Furuhjelm led a discussion at the 2014 LSFMM Summit on SMR drives, explaining device-managed, host-aware, and host-managed types with sequential zone requirements and new SCSI commands for zone reporting.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591779/][Persistent memory]]: Matthew Wilcox and Kent Overstreet discussed DAX (direct access) block layer for persistent memory at the 2014 LSFMM Summit, allowing filesystems to access persistent storage without page caching, along with msync() and mmap() improvements.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591777/][Linux 3.14-rc8]]: Linus Torvalds released Linux 3.14-rc8 with VFS fixes detected by Trinity, networking fixes, and plans for the final 3.14 release the following weekend.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591961/][Compressed swap]]: Bob Liu discussed zswap performance problems at the 2014 LSFMM Summit, where zbud pool eviction requires decompression and writing to swap, and Mel Gorman emphasized the need for better benchmark workloads before any changes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591978/][Memory management locking]]: Davidlohr Bueso led a session at the 2014 LSFMM Summit on rwsem spinning improvements and anon_vma lock issues, while discussing mmap_sem contention and converting callers to get_user_pages_fast().
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591979/][Hardware pain points for memory management]]: H. Peter Anvin led a session at the 2014 LSFMM Summit gathering hardware wishes for memory management, including TLB flush functions, 64KB page support on x86, fast page zeroing, and faster iret for page faults.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592042/][Volatile ranges]]: At the 2014 LSFMM Summit, developers discussed volatile ranges and MADV_FREE APIs, addressing questions about vrange() vs madvise() interfaces, page purging information, and use cases for graphics drivers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591985/][Toward better testing]]: Dave Chinner and Dave Jones led a discussion on testing tools at the 2014 LSFMM Summit, covering xfstests coverage, power-failure testing, performance regression testing needs, and the lack of testing culture in the kernel community.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591990/][User-space out-of-memory handling]]: David Rientjes presented user-space OOM handling patches at the 2014 LSFMM Summit, but the community was divided between using vmpressure vs user-space handlers, with concerns about memcg coupling and lack of consensus on moving OOM policy to user space.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591995/][NUMA placement problems]]: Rik van Riel, Peter Zijlstra, and Mel Gorman led a session at the 2014 LSFMM Summit on NUMA placement, noting that automatic placement works on 4-node systems but degrades on larger systems, with no clear understanding of why page hinting costs are problematic.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591998/][Memory compaction issues]]: Vlastimil Babka led a session at the 2014 LSFMM Summit on memory compaction problems, discussing compaction overhead and the difficulty of creating test programs that reveal compaction issues due to specific workload access patterns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592011/][Huge page issues]]: At the 2014 LSFMM Summit, developers discussed transparent huge page complexity, with Andrew Morton saying it has made a mess of the kernel, and Kirill Shutemov presented work on extending huge pages to page cache with reference counting solutions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592045/][Memory accounting and limits]]: At the 2014 LSFMM Summit, Michal Hocko proposed low limits for memcgs as a memory guarantee, while Peter Zijlstra discussed reverting pinned page accounting to count against mlock limits to prevent processes pushing systems into OOM.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/592051/][Dirty pages, faster writing and fsync]]: Discussion on PostgreSQL pain points related to fsync() behavior, with ext3 being the outlier that syncs all dirty blocks filesystem-wide rather than just the specific file.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591391/][Fedora Present and Future: a Fedora.next 2014 Update (Part I, "Why?")]]: Matthew Miller's Fedora.next update explains why Linux distributions are declining in popularity and announces plans to restructure Fedora around three core areas: Environments, Stacks, and Base Design.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591420/][The new and the not new in Java 8]]: Java 8 launched with lambda expressions for functional programming, parallel Stream API, and Project Nashorn JavaScript engine, while Jigsaw modularization and Stripped Implementations were delayed to Java 9.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591977/][Mozilla's "rr" debugger]]: Mozilla released rr, a record-and-replay debugger that enables monotonic debugging progression with lower overhead than gdb's reverse execution, allowing debugging of complex applications like Firefox.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591702/][Does the Display Server matter?]]: Robert Ancell argued toolkits abstract display server differences, but Martin Gräßlin countered with concrete examples of toolkit-specific behavior issues between Wayland and X11.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590557/][IPython and its Notebook]]: IPython is an enhanced interactive Python REPL with features like history editing, syntax highlighting, tab completion, and matplotlib integration; the IPython Notebook provides web-based interactive documents for data visualization and teaching.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590863/][Shuttleworth: ACPI, firmware and your security]]: Mark Shuttleworth argues that ACPI is a security hole given NSA firmware exploits revealed by Snowden, calling firmware a cesspool of insecurity from manufacturers and government agencies alike.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590991/][Volatile ranges and MADV_FREE]]: John Stultz's vrange() system call and Minchan Kim's MADV_FREE madvise() command provide ways to mark memory regions as volatile, allowing the kernel to reclaim them under memory pressure while applications can handle the result.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590928/][SO_PEERCGROUP: which container is calling?]]: Vivek Goyal proposed SO_PEERCGROUP getsockopt() to let daemons like SSSD determine which container a connecting process belongs to, sparking debate about cgroups vs user namespaces as the right approach.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590960/][User-space out-of-memory handling]]: David Rientjes proposed user-space OOM handling allowing processes to receive eventfd() notifications when memory is tight and configure memory reserves via memory.oom_control and memory.oom_reserve_in_bytes control files.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/591001/][Functional Programming in Java--New from Pragmatic Bookshelf]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf announces 'Functional Programming in Java' by Venkat Subramaniam, covering lambda expressions, method references, and functional interfaces in Java 8.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590156/][What's new with HTTP2]]: HTTP2 draft version 10 adds multiplexing, header compression, and server push to HTTP, aiming to reduce latency while maintaining HTTP 1.1 semantics, with discussion of encryption requirements.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590299/][A false midnight]]: Python's datetime.time(0,0,0) evaluates to False due to UTC midnight being treated as zero, sparking discussion about changing this behavior for consistency with other time values.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589147/][The status of Wayland security]]: Wayland provides better input/output security than X but needs mechanisms like Wayland Security Modules (WSMs) to allow users to authorize restricted clients like screen readers and screen lockers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590214/][A discussion between database and kernel developers]]: Mel Gorman announced a meeting between database and kernel developers at Collaboration Summit 2014 to discuss pain points like IO scheduling, NUMA optimization, and memory management issues affecting PostgreSQL and other databases.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590378/][Unmixing the pool]]: Kernel developers discussed updates to random number generation entropy pools, including adding RDSEED support and debated whether mixing hardware RNG output into the pool without entropy credit is safe.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590243/][MCS locks and qspinlocks]]: New locking mechanisms (MCS locks and qspinlocks) were merged to reduce cache-line bouncing for highly contended spinlocks, improving kernel performance especially for disk-intensive workloads.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590296/][A setuid wrapper for X.org]]: Hans de Goede proposed a setuid wrapper allowing X.org to run as an unprivileged user when kernel mode setting (KMS) is available, enhancing security while maintaining compatibility with binary drivers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590311/][Bits from the Security Team]]: Debian Security Team meeting summary covering security tracker automation, release workflow changes, LTS support for Squeeze, and distribution hardening initiatives including hidepid and stack protection improvements.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590381/][Glibc feature test macros]]: Michael Kerrisk explained how feature test macros control header definitions in glibc, covering standards-related FTMs, the deprecation of _BSD_SOURCE and _SVID_SOURCE, and common pitfalls with macro ordering.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590231/][Is parallel programming hard?, first edition]]: Paul McKenney announced the first edition of his 500-page book on parallel programming, released under CC-BY-SA 3.0 license with topics covering kernel synchronization and concurrency patterns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/590301/][Sneak Preview of oSC14 Sessions]]: Preview of openSUSE Conference 2014 sessions covering ownCloud, KDE desktop updates, MySQL databases, and Jolla phone development.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589137/][Progress toward free GPU drivers]]: NVIDIA and Broadcom made significant strides toward open-source GPU drivers, with Broadcom releasing VideoCore documentation and driver stack under BSD license for Raspberry Pi and other SoC products.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589196/][Using git and make for tasks beyond coding]]: Don Marti demonstrated using makefiles and git hooks for document processing automation at SCALE 12x, including Pandoc conversions and automated spell-checking workflows.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589205/][A longstanding GnuTLS certificate validation botch]]: Critical bug in GnuTLS certificate validation allowed crafted certificates to pass checks due to incorrect return values in check_if_ca(), affecting all versions since 2000.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589291/][Critical crypto bug leaves Linux, hundreds of apps open to eavesdropping]]: Ars Technica reported on the GnuTLS certificate validation vulnerability similar to Apple goto fail bug, exposing many Linux applications to man-in-the-middle attacks.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589183/][Red Hat's dynamic kernel patching project]]: Red Hat announced kpatch, a live kernel patching project similar to ksplice and SUSE's kGraft, allowing administrators to apply security patches without reboots.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589260/][Finding the proper scope of a file collapse operation]]: Kernel developers discussed adding FALLOC_FL_COLLAPSE_RANGE to fallocate() for efficient video editing by removing file segments without copying data.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/588799/][Tracing unsigned modules]]: Mathieu Desnoyers proposed adding TAINT_UNSIGNED_MODULE flag to distinguish unsigned modules from forced modules, allowing tracepoints to work with unsigned modules.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589009/][A JIT for grepping: jrep and rejit]]: Alexandre Rames introduced jrep, a JIT-compiling grep replacement powered by the rejit library, showing significant performance improvements over GNU grep on complex regex patterns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/589105/][What is good video editing software on Linux?]]: Xmodulo overview of ten Linux video editors with discussion highlighting Kdenlive and Blender as the most viable options for daily use.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/588451/][What Linux and Solaris can learn from each other]]: Brendan Gregg's SCALE 12x keynote comparing Linux and SmartOS performance analysis tools, covering DTrace, ZFS, resource controls, and profiling differences between the systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/588309/][Seven problems with Linux containers]]: Kirill Kolyshkin's SCALE 12x talk covering OpenVZ container challenges including resource controls, live migration, upstreaming to mainline kernel, filesystem bottlenecks, and storage efficiency.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/588369/][goto fail; considered harmful]]: Analysis of Apple's critical SSL/TLS verification bug where a duplicate goto fail; line unconditionally skipped certificate validation in SecureTransport API.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/587404/][Peres: Wayland Compositors - Why and How to Handle Privileged Clients!]]: Martin Peres discussed security in Wayland compositors, recommending user-intent and static privilege assignment methods for handling privileged clients.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/588086/][Deferrable timers for user space]]: Thomas Gleixner proposed adding deferrable timer support (TIMER_IS_DEFERRABLE/TFD_TIMER_IS_DEFERRABLE flags) to clock_nanosleep() and timerfd_settime() for power efficiency.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/588300/][C11 atomics part 2: consume semantics]]: Discussion of C11 consume memory ordering semantics for RCU, Linus proposed simplifying consume semantics definition to pointer chain tracking rather than full dependency tracking.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/588444/][Proper handling of unknown flags in system calls]]: Michael Kerrisk explained importance of validating unknown flags in system calls to return EINVAL and future-proof APIs for backward compatibility.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/587923/][PyPy and software transactional memory]]: PyPy project progress on STM using remap_file_pages() for parallel execution without GIL, showing 15-50% single-thread slowdown instead of 2-5x.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/587580/][Kügler: Next means Focus on the Core]]: KDE Plasma Next preview emphasizing visual improvements, cleaner workflows, and better usability while maintaining user customization options.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/588249/][Servo: Inside Mozilla's mission to reinvent the web browser]]: Mozilla's Servo browser engine written in Rust aims to parallelize layout, rendering, and JavaScript execution across multiple cores.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/586427/][Adding CPU randomness to the entropy pool]]: Kernel developers discussed Jörn Engel's CPU randomness patch and Stephan Müller's CPU Jitter RNG for improving entropy during early boot without entropy credit.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/586904/][File-private POSIX locks]]: A proposed new type of POSIX lock that combines BSD-style and POSIX lock semantics to be more threading-friendly, where locks are owned by the open file description rather than the process, solving problems like locks being dropped when any fd to the file is closed.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/586838/][C11 atomic variables and the kernel]]: Discussion of the challenges and concerns around using C11 standard atomic variables in the Linux kernel, including compiler optimization worries about speculative stores, control dependencies, and whether the kernel really needs them given its existing memory barrier infrastructure.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/586444/][How OpenStack parallels the adoption of Linux (opensource.com)]]: Red Hat's cloud evangelist Gordon Haff compares OpenStack adoption patterns to Linux adoption, noting that like Linux, OpenStack wins through lower cost and vendor choice rather than raw technology superiority.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/585439/][Controlling device power management]]: A kernel mechanism (latency tolerance device pm_qos) that allows the system to communicate latency requirements to devices with internal power management, telling them not to enter sleep states that would take longer to wake from than the specified tolerance.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/585415/][Flags as a system call API design pattern]]: A discussion of how system calls should include flags arguments from the start to avoid needing new versions like dup2/dup3 and pipe/pipe2, using renameat2 as a recent example of learning this lesson the hard way.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/585782/][Best practices for a big patch series]]: Guidance on submitting large cross-subsystem patch series, covering organization strategies (whole-tree, per-file, per-directory), merge procedures, and using get_maintainer.pl for proper CC handling.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/584176/][Systemd programming part 2: activation and language issues]]: Second part examining systemd from a programming language perspective, covering service activation mechanisms (events vs dependencies reversed from upstart), language syntax issues with conditionals and the many overlapping dependency directives.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/584629/][Jones: The EFI System Partition and the Default Boot Behavior]]: Blog post explaining UEFI boot process, describing EFI System Partition requirements, BootOrder variable usage, and how firmware falls back to removable media boot.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/585775/][New from No Starch Press: "Learn to Program with Scratch"]]: Press release announcing a new book by Majed Marji teaching programming concepts using Scratch's visual block-based language, aimed at beginners including students and educators.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/584225/]["Strong" stack protection for GCC]]: Description of GCC 4.9's new -fstack-protector-strong option that provides broader stack buffer overflow protection than regular (only catches 8+ byte char arrays) without the performance hit of protecting all functions, adopted in Linux 3.14 kernel.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/584020/][An x32 local exploit]]: Details of a serious local privilege escalation bug in the x32 ABI's recvmmsg() implementation where a user-space pointer was incorrectly treated as a kernel pointer, allowing unprivileged users to gain root; the bug existed for two years before discovery.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/584123/][ARM, SBSA, UEFI, and ACPI]]: Discussion of ARM's Server Base System Architecture (SBSA) for standardizing server hardware, and the controversy around mandating UEFI and ACPI firmware which some developers fear will repeat the x86 ACPI compatibility噩梦.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/584175/][Systemd programming part 1: modularity and configuration]]: First of two articles examining systemd from a programming language perspective, covering modularity (unit files vs SysVinit scripts) and configuration challenges like optional command-line arguments and drop-in files.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/582697/][GCC, LLVM, and compiler plugins]]: Discussion of GCC vs LLVM development approaches, the debate over whether GCC should adopt LLVM's modular architecture, and Stallman's insistence that GCC's GPL-based plugin policy is essential to its mission.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/583171/][Spoiled onions and Tor exit relays]]: Karlstad University research finding that about 2.5% of Tor exit relays were conducting malicious activities including HTTPS MITM attacks, SSL stripping, DNS poisoning, and HTML injection over a four-month study period.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/583187/][Alkema: Misconceptions about forward-secrecy]]: Blog post debunking forward secrecy misconceptions, including that more encryption keys mean better security and that forward secrecy protects against all future decryption attempts.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/584175/][Systemd programming part 1: modularity and configuration]]: First of two articles examining systemd from a programming language perspective, covering modularity (unit files vs SysVinit scripts) and configuration challenges like optional command-line arguments and drop-in files.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/582697/][GCC, LLVM, and compiler plugins]]: Discussion of GCC vs LLVM development approaches, the debate over whether GCC should adopt LLVM's modular architecture, and Stallman's insistence that GCC's GPL-based plugin policy is essential to its mission.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/583171/][Spoiled onions and Tor exit relays]]: Karlstad University research finding that about 2.5% of Tor exit relays were conducting malicious activities including HTTPS MITM attacks, SSL stripping, DNS poisoning, and HTML injection over a four-month study period.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/583187/][Alkema: Misconceptions about forward-secrecy]]: Blog post debunking forward secrecy misconceptions, including that more encryption keys mean better security and that forward secrecy protects against all future decryption attempts.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/582862/][Preparing for large-sector drives]]: Discussion of kernel challenges supporting drives with 64KB sectors (coming in 2-3 years), including page cache issues requiring either higher-order page allocations or major VM changes, versus relying on firmware RMW emulation.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/581086/][FreeOTP multi-factor authentication]]: Red Hat's open-source replacement for Google Authenticator (discontinued as open source), providing HOTP/TOTP two-factor authentication with mobile apps for Android and iOS, recommended for use with FreeIPA.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/580814/][Kroah-Hartman: Kdbus Details]]: Blog post clarifying kdbus details, explaining why it won't replace Android's binder IPC (binder is more efficient for low-memory devices) and noting kdbus userspace will live in systemd repo.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/581558/][Btrfs: Send/receive and ioctl()]]: Final article in LWN's Btrfs series covering send/receive for efficient incremental backups between Btrfs filesystems, and Btrfs-specific ioctl() commands including file cloning and experimental transaction handling.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/580893/][Namespaces in operation, part 7: Network namespaces]]: Seventh in LWN namespace series covering network namespaces which partition network devices, addresses, ports, routes and firewall rules; includes setup with ip netns, veth pairs for cross-namespace communication, and security isolation use cases.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/581475/][Of bytes and encoded strings]]: Python 3 string handling discussion covering PEP 460/461 for bytes formatting, the bytes vs str separation debate, and Guido van Rossum's decision to allow b'%d' % 42 in Python 3.5 for practical over pure reasons.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/580451/][Supporting connected standby]]: Matthew Garrett's LCA 2014 talk on Linux challenges with connected standby (always-on low-power mode), covering timer slack as solution for preventing unnecessary wakeups, RCU issues, and user-space power management problems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/580186/][Standardizing virtio]]: Rusty Russell's LCA 2014 talk on virtio standardization through OASIS, covering virtio 1.0 spec changes including endianness (now little-endian), VIRTIO_F_VERSION_1 flag, virtqueue layout improvements, and removal of virtio-balloon from standard.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/580194/][The unveiling of kdbus]]: Lennart Poettering's LCA 2014 talk introducing kdbus - a kernel-based D-Bus implementation providing zero-copy messaging, memfds for large data, Bloom filters for signals, and 2-copy worst case vs user-space D-Bus's 10-copy/4-context-switch overhead.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/580399/][Python packaging: playing well with others]]: Nick Coghlan's LCA 2014 talk on Python packaging improvements including pip adoption in 3.4, wheel binary format, warehouse replacement for PyPI, end-to-end signing (PEP 458), and PEP 440 versioning system.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/580597/][Clasen: client-side decoration, continued]]: Brief overview of GNOME's new window titlebar approach making titlebar space usable by applications rather than just holding title and window buttons.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/579469/][Deciphering Google's automotive Android plan]]: Analysis of Open Auto Alliance (OAA) announcement at CES 2014 - seems focused on Android phone/car IVI tethering rather than full Android-IVI integration, with Google joining existing consortia like GENIVI.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/579044/][A crypto library aimed at auditability]]: TweetNaCl is a compact (16KB), auditable cryptographic library based on NaCl that provides strong security through modern algorithms (Salsa20, Poly1305, Curve25519), designed for projects that need verifiable crypto implementations rather than feature-rich toolkits.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/578852/][Understanding the Jailhouse hypervisor, part 2]]: Second part explaining Jailhouse's LAPIC virtualization for interrupt isolation, cell creation by shrinking Linux's resources, and hypervisor shutdown through VMXOFF on each CPU.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/579009/][Btrfs: Subvolumes and snapshots]]: Btrfs subvolumes function as independent mountable filesystems while snapshots provide copy-on-write point-in-time backups, with quota groups available though enforcement remains imprecise.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/578842/][Raymond: bzr is dying; Emacs needs to move]]: Eric Raymond argues Emacs should migrate from Bazaar to Git, citing bzr's moribund development and Canonical's shift to Git, with RMS showing unexpected openness to the change.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/579684/][Heilmann: Endangered species of the Web: the Link]]: Chris Heilmann's critique of modern web practices that endanger proper URL links, calling out javascript:void(0), hashbang URLs, shortlinks, and other link-killing patterns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/578190/][Huang: On Hacking MicroSD Cards]]: Bunnie Huang's analysis revealing that MicroSD cards contain hackable firmware-running microcontrollers capable of MITM attacks, warning that secure-erase is insufficient for sensitive data.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/577961/][Btrfs: Working with multiple devices]]: Btrfs's built-in RAID support for combining multiple devices with configurable redundancy (single, raid0, raid1, raid10, raid5, raid6) and independent metadata/data settings.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/578295/][Understanding the Jailhouse hypervisor, part 1]]: Introduction to Jailhouse - a lightweight partitioning hypervisor that cooperates with Linux to isolate bare-metal applications in cells using VT-x/VT-d hardware virtualization.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/578304/][Gaynor: About Python 3]]: Alex Gaynor argues the Python 2/3 split has led to lethargic adoption of Python 3 due to lack of urgency and the absence of major improvements like GIL removal.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/577370/][Simple wait queues]]: Linux kernel simplification effort to replace complex wait queues with Thomas Gleixner's "simple wait queue" (swait) mechanism, returning to 2.0-style linked lists without exclusive waits or callbacks.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/577164/][A proposal for "silent" port knocking]]: GNUnet proposal to add TCP_STEALTH option for in-kernel port knocking using sequence number encoding; met with skepticism from network developers preferring user-space solutions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/577218/][Btrfs: Getting started]]: Introduction to Btrfs basics - filesystem creation, mounting with compression/COW options, tools (mkfs.btrfs, btrfsck, scrub), and the state of btrfs-progs v3.12.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/577593/][The Android AppOps vanishing act]]: Android 4.3 added AppOps per-app permission controls, but 4.4.2 removed them claiming experimental; third-party ROMs like CyanogenMod restored the feature.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/577570/][Breaking Python's API]]: Python 2.7.6 changed undocumented randrange() parameters (int, maxwidth → _int, _maxwidth), breaking ZODB; controversy over point-release API changes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/576965/][Packard: Cleaning up X server warnings]]: Keith Packard cleaned up X server compiler warnings - old pre-ANSI C code without prototypes or const; targeted for X server 1.15 release.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/576564/][A multiprocess Firefox]]: Mozilla Electrolysis project enabled multiprocess Firefox (UI + content processes); initially all tabs in one content process with IPC message passing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/576545/][Cook: live patching the kernel]]: Kees Cook's manual kernel patching to disable kexec by borrowing PaX's KERNEXEC technique (disable WP bit briefly); followed by disabling module loading for permanent lockdown.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/576276/][The Btrfs filesystem: An introduction]]: Comprehensive Btrfs overview - copy-on-write design, snapshots, volume manager, checksumming, compression; development statistics showing steady activity at ~670 changesets/year from 68 developers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575846/][Fixing FS_IOC_GETFLAGS]]: Linux ioctl() ABI issue - FS_IOC_GETFLAGS/SETFLAGS expect 32-bit int on both 32/64-bit systems; big-endian 64-bit machines see wrong bytes due to long* definition.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/576486/][Memory barriers for TSO architectures]]: New smp_load_acquire() and smp_store_release() barriers for TSO architectures (x86) - enables weaker barriers for lockless ring buffer code; ~half of explicit barriers could be replaced.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/576473/]["We cannot trust" Intel and Via's chip-based crypto, FreeBSD developers say]]: FreeBSD 10 won't trust RDRAND/Padlock directly; passes hardware RNG output through Yarrow algorithm to prevent potential hardware backdoors from affecting /dev/random.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/576478/][Returning EINTR from close()]]: Linux close() always succeeds (fd deallocated early); EINTR return is impossible on Linux. glibc may map EINTR→EINPROGRESS or 0 since retrying close() is dangerous.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575830/][McCloskey: Multiprocess Firefox]]: Firefox Electrolysis architecture using OMTC (off main thread compositing) with separate browser/content processes communicating via IPC message passing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/576482/][Build Awesome Command-Line Applications in Ruby 2]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf announcement for Ruby CLI programming book by David B. Copeland (222 pages, $30).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575672/][Another daemon for managing control groups]]: Serge Hallyn's cgmanager daemon for cgroup management via D-Bus - alternative to systemd's cgroup management for non-systemd distributions like Ubuntu using Upstart.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575531/][BPF tracing filters]]: Alexei Starovoitov's extended BPF (Berkeley Packet Filter) virtual machine for kernel tracing filters - allows unprivileged users to load safe programs, compiled from C to native machine code.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575460/][A surprise with mutexes and reference counts]]: Linux mutex implementation bug where spinning waiters can acquire lock before unlock completes - leads to use-after-free if mutex protects refcount that triggers kfree.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575497/][Deadline scheduling: coming soon?]]: SCHED_DEADLINE patch set by Juri Lelli - EDF (Earliest Deadline First) scheduling replacing priorities with runtime/period/deadline parameters; new sched_attr structure and sched_setscheduler2 syscall.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575493/][A Rust frontend for GCC]]: Philip Herron's gccrs project - Rust frontend for GCC (gccrs branch); compiles basic Rust code (structs, impl blocks, while loops, functions) to GIMPLE after ~1 month of development.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575520/][Node.js the Right Way]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf announcement - Jim R. Wilson's Node.js server-side JavaScript book covering async programming, npm modules, protocols, REST services, 100 pages, $17.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575677/][Perl One-Liners]]: No Starch Press announcement - Peteris Krumins' "Perl One-Liners" book with 130 compact Perl programs for automation tasks, 168 pages, $24.95.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/574676/][A Summer Spent on the LLVM Clang Static Analyzer for the Linux Kernel]]: Google Summer of Code project by Eduard Bachmakov - LLVM Clang static analyzer for kernel with checker tool generating HTML reports showing error paths through code.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/574946/][Seigo: Introducing Improv]]: Aaron Seigo's $75 development board with dual-core ARM Cortex-A7, 1GB RAM, 4GB NAND, OpenGL ES GPU, running Mer OS - community-focused open hardware with EOMA68 modular connector.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/575064/][Functional Programming Patterns in Scala and Clojure]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book by Michael Bevilacqua-Linn - compares OOP patterns with functional alternatives in Scala and Clojure for JVM developers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/573952/][GNU virtual private Ethernet]]: GVPE v2.25 - VPN creating actual Ethernet network between multiple nodes rather than point-to-point tunnels; uses EC DH key exchange, compile-time cipher selection, supports raw IP/UDP/TCP/ICMP/DNS transport.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/573834/][Your visual how-to guide for SELinux policy enforcement]]: Dan Walsh's opensource.com tutorial using dogs/cats analogy with Máirín Duffy's cartoons to explain type enforcement, MCS, and MLS concepts.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/574274/][The "Jailhouse" hypervisor]]: Linux-native partitioning hypervisor like KVM but for isolating bare-metal apps in cells on dedicated CPUs using VT-x/VT-d hardware virtualization.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/574317/][The past, present, and future of control groups]]: Tejun Heo's Korea Linux Forum talk on cgroup mistakes (missing hierarchy support, release_agent, VFS entanglement), and plans for cgroup v2 API with unified hierarchy.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/573409/][Device trees II: The harder parts]]: Neil Brown's second devicetree article covering cross-tree linkages for interrupts (interrupt-parent), GPIOs (gpios attribute), regulators, and pinctrl; discusses EPROBE_DEFER for deferred probing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/574215/][The failure of pysandbox]]: Victor Stinner admits pysandbox (CPython sandbox) is fundamentally broken - too many introspection escape routes; whole Python core is attack surface; compile() and traceback exploits; recommends external sandboxing (seccomp).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/573837/][Dart 1.0: A stable SDK for structured web apps]]: Google announces Dart 1.0 SDK release - language for web apps compiling to JavaScript, with simple yet powerful language, tools, and core libraries.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/573988/][Four years of Go]]: Go language 4-year retrospective - phenomenal open source ecosystem, compared to Python in 1995 or Java in 1999; discussion of git vs mercurial philosophy.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/574280/][Exploring LXC Networking]]: containerops.org tutorial on LXC container networking - various network configurations and management within and around LXC containers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572692/][Device trees I: Are we having fun yet?]]: Neil Brown's introduction to device trees for ARM - explains why ARM has no standard platform like PC BIOS, devicetree as hardware description, comparison with board files, example from GTA04 phone.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/573424/][User-space RCU]]: Paul McKenney, Mathieu Desnoyers, Lai Jiangshan describe liburcu - user-space RCU library with 5 flavors (QSBR, RCU_MEMBARRIER, RCU_SIGNAL, RCU_MB, bullet-proof); provides RCU-protected hash tables, stacks, queues.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/573695/][Ruby Under a Microscope]]: No Starch Press book by Pat Shaughnessy - illustrated guide to Ruby internals covering Ruby 2.0 garbage collection, YARV compiler, method lookup, how classes/modules are same inside Ruby.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572598/][Automotive networking]]: Linux in cars - SocketCAN for CAN bus, NFC for pairing/keyless entry, Bluetooth HFP/AVRCP for hands-free/audio, 802.11p for V2V/V2I vehicle networking; no upstream 802.11p driver yet.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572926/][Let's talk about perfect forward secrecy]]: Nathan Willis explains PFS - protecting past sessions if current key is compromised; DHE/ECDHE provide PFS; SSH, OTR, IPsec have it; most HTTPS lacks it; June 2013 Netcraft survey found only Google used PFS among major sites.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/573092/][Support for atomic block I/O operations]]: Chris Mason's O_ATOMIC|O_DIRECT flags for atomic multi-block writes - hardware either writes all blocks or none; target is MySQL to halve writes by disabling double buffering.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572911/][The pernicious USB-stick stall problem]]: Writing to slow USB devices hangs entire system - 64-bit kernel allows 3.2GB dirty limit vs 180MB on 32-bit; Linus proposes limiting percentage-based calculations to first 1GB of memory.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572740/][The future of realtime Linux]]: Thomas Gleixner reports PREEMPT_RT status at RTLWS 2013 - 95% upstream, 5% remains; needs 4-5 full-time developers; either gets remaining code upstream or project declared done in 2014.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572957/][Creating containers with systemd-nspawn]]: Lennart Poettering's LinuxCon Europe talk - systemd-nspawn is "chroot on steroids" for building/testing/debugging; uses machinectl for container management, journal integration for logging, optional private network isolation.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/571934/][The kernel/user-space boundary]]: 2013 Kernel Summit discussion - Linus emphasized "don't break user space" policy; 2GB I/O limit justified for security; pty/container issues unresolved; tracepoint ABI concerns; printk() is not an ABI but changes will be fixed if they break scripts.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/571977/][The evolution of control groups]]: Tejun Heo presented cgroup unified hierarchy plans at Kernel Summit - multiple hierarchies being removed; per-process (not per-thread) control; old ABI will be maintained 10+ years; systemd delegation concerns; Google admitted it can probably make the transition.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572068/][Git tree maintenance]]: tip tree (Thomas Gleixner, Ingo Molnar, Peter Anvin) and arm-soc tree management - topic/urgent/queue branches; tip-bot notifications; arm-soc has 150 merges per cycle; drivers moving to mainline.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572114/][Device tree bindings]]: Grant Likely and David Woodhouse - device tree bindings are stable ABI by default; configuration data allowed; unstable bindings staging mechanism; compatibility rules: new kernels work with older device trees.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572125/][Checkpoint/restart in user space]]: CRIU (Checkpoint/Restart in User Space) working in 3.11 - almost entirely user-space with minimal kernel additions; supports live migration; Pavel Emelyanov requests: query APIs for new resources, per-process IDs not global.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572150/][High Performance Drupal]]: O'Reilly book announcement - practical techniques for scaling Drupal sites.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572151/][Super Scratch Programming Adventure]]: No Starch Press book - Scratch programming for kids using game examples.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/572152/][3D Game Programming for Kids]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book - interactive 3D programming using JavaScript.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/571266/][Building APIs on top of GStreamer]]: GStreamer Editing Services (GES) for nonlinear video editing - GESTimeline, GESLayer, effects API, keyframes; FluMediaPlayer from Fluendo for simple playback; GStreamer 1.0 API stability.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/570369/][Web fonts, open source, and industry disruption]]: ATypI 2013 conference - Google Fonts (139.5B uses of Open Sans) disrupting typography; type designers concerned about $6500 flat fees for font families; business models shifting; open fonts gaining acceptance.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/570471/][Rationalizing Python packaging]]: PEP 453 adoption - pip becoming official Python package manager; ensurepip module for 3.4; bundled pip in Python distribution; setuptools eventually deprecated; Python 2.7 no ensurepip (no new features policy).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/570353/][A new direction for power-aware scheduling]]: Morten Rasmussen's power-aware scheduling patches - new power_driver API replacing cpuidle/cpufreq; at_max_capacity(), go_faster(), go_slower() methods; scheduler idle integration; long-term plan: eliminate cpufreq/cpuidle entirely.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/570558/][Deploying Docker]]: Container deployment using Docker - lightweight containerization platform.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/570469/][PyPy's new garbage collector]]: Incremental GC in PyPy - splitting major collections to avoid long pauses; problem: marking with pointer changes during GC.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/570381/][Real World Cryptography Workshop]]: Workshop on applied cryptography.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569688/][The Thing System]]: Home automation project - steward process on Node.js; supports diverse devices via SSDP/Bluetooth/USB; ten device types; Simple Thing Protocol for vendor APIs; activity-based scripting.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569635/][Kernel address space layout randomization]]: KASLR - kernel address space layout randomization for security.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569686/][Optimizing CPU hotplug locking]]: Peter Zijlstra's CPU hotplug locking optimization - per-CPU reference counts replace mutex; three states (readers_fast/slow/block); rcu_sync primitive to avoid synchronize_sched() calls; common case is fast per-CPU increment.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569795/][Fedora's working groups]]: Fedora project reorganization into working groups - modular governance structure.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569787/][Firefox Developer Tools and Firebug]]: Firefox developer tools improvements - Web IDE, debugger, console upgrades.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569272/][Garrett: The state of XMir]]: Matthew Garrett's assessment - Ubuntu's XMir development driven by phone needs; XMir has unique requirements no other Mir client needs; Canonical needs to resolve issues for shipping.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569634/][White paper: the economic value of the Long Term Support Initiative]]: Linux Foundation white paper on LTSI value.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569083/][The history of Mesa]]: History of Mesa 3D graphics library - from SGI to open source.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569180/][TT-RSS makes a comeback]]: Tiny Tiny RSS feed reader - self-hosted alternative to Google Reader.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/568943/][Integrity and embedded devices]]: Embedded device integrity - secure boot and measurement.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569134/][Exchanging two files]]: Atomic file exchange methods.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/568984/][Transactional memory in the dentry cache]]: Dcache transaction patches - filesystem name resolution caching with transactional semantics.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/568891/][How much memory power management is useful?]]: Memory power management effectiveness - how much power can be saved.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/568870/][NUMA scheduling progress]]: NUMA scheduling improvements - better placement of tasks on NUMA systems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/568517/][Pasting images with automatic attribution]]: Image paste with attribution - content identification for pasted images.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/569189/][Practical Programming, 2nd Edition]]: Pragmatic Bookshelf book - Python programming tutorial.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/564944/][Chromatic fonts are coming]]: Chromatic fonts - multi-color font technology.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/565113/][Binary "diversity"]]: Binary diversity in software - multiple implementations for security.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/564368/][Perry: Deterministic Builds Part One]]: Deterministic builds - cyberwar and global compromise context.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/565121/][flink() flunks]]: flink() syscall failure - filesystem link operations.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/564978/][TSO sizing and the FQ scheduler]]: TCP Segmentation Offload sizing with FQ scheduler.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/564854/][Device namespaces]]: Device namespace isolation for containers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/565097/][Cramming more into struct page]]: Kernel struct page expansion - memory management changes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/565032/][Embedding OS/X UI elements in the GTK+ toolkit]]: Embedding native UI in GTK+ - platform integration.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/565115/][A Compleat Historye of ye Anti-harassment Policies]]: Anti-harassment policies history in open source communities.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/564988/][Python in Practice]]: New book announcement - Python programming advanced topics.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641779/][The programming talent myth]]: Jacob Kaplan-Moss PyCon 2015 keynote - challenging the myth of rock star programmers; programming skill follows normal distribution, most people are average; talent myth keeps people from learning programming; encourages embracing being "average" to make programming less intimidating.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642166/][Random numbers from CPU execution time jitter]]: Stephan Müller's CPU jitter RNG patch - uses execution time variation as entropy source for kernel random number generation; addresses entropy starvation in embedded/virtual environments; debate continues about entropy quality estimates.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642065/][Garrett: Reducing power consumption on Haswell and Broadwell systems]]: Matthew Garrett's investigation - reduced idle power from 8.5W to 5W on his laptop by configuring Intel chipset defaults properly; lack of integration between kernel power management and firmware settings; distributions need to figure out appropriate defaults.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642069/][Pagemap: security fixes vs. ABI compatibility]]: Discussion of /proc/kpageidle and /proc/kpagecgroup interfaces - tracking actual page usage for memory control groups; privileged access required for tracking physical page idle state; kernel patch to provide better memory utilization information.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642202/][Tracking actual memory utilization]]: Vladimir Davydov's patch adding /proc/kpageidle and /proc/kpagecgroup - allows monitoring actual page usage vs. resident set size; helps with container memory partitioning and memcg limits; uses new idle/young page flags to avoid perturbing page reclaim.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641790/][Rust Once, Run Everywhere]]: Rust FFI guide - using Rust's safe abstractions to interface with C code; ownership and borrowing principles make APIs safer than C; zero overhead bindings; discussion of unsafe blocks and sandboxing limitations.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640302/][Plotting tools for networks, part II]]: Lee Phillips article - TikZ/PGF LaTeX package for embedded diagrams with graph drawing algorithms (tree, force-directed); NetworkX Python library for network analysis and visualization; GML format for network data; shortest path calculations with weighted edges.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640838/][Adding Requests to the standard library]]: Kenneth Reitz proposal at Python Language Summit - Requests module too critical to be in standard library due to fast security update cycle; dependencies (chardet, urllib3) would also need inclusion; conclusion: keep Requests on PyPI rather than stdlib.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641103/][Jython Native Interface (JyNI)]]: Stefan Richthofer's JyNI project - enables Jython to use Python C extensions; adapts Python C API to Java Native Interface; biggest challenge is garbage collection between JVM and native code.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641247/][Taking control of SSDs with LightNVM]]: Matias Bjørling's LightNVM patch set - allows kernel to bypass flash translation layer in SSDs; provides open-channel SSD interface for better performance; includes RRPC FTL implementation; aim is to let kernel manage flash directly.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641275/][The kdbuswreck]]: Jonathan Corbet's analysis of kdbus debate - D-Bus protocol implementation in kernel; controversy over capability metadata passing with messages; Andy Lutomirski's objections to capability-based authentication; user namespace compatibility issues; Linus staying out of debate.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641435/][Encryption, the NSA, and the front door]]: Nathan Willis on NSA director's split-key escrow proposal - similar to 1990s Clipper chip; government would hold half of encryption keys; criticism about keeping key halves separate; concerns about making US software companies uncompetitive; EFF comparing to past failed key escrow attempts.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/638636/][Stenberg: The state and rate of HTTP/2 adoption]]: Daniel Stenberg's blog post - HTTP/2 adoption analysis covering browsers, servers, proxies, CDNs; predictions for >10% usage by end of 2015, majority by 2016.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/597895/][Defeating memory comparison timing oracles (Red Hat Security Blog)]]: Florian Weimer examines timing oracles in memory comparison functions like memcmp() that can allow attackers to extract secret data by measuring execution time differences. The article discusses Red Hat's research into making memcmp() oracle-free by processing data in larger chunks (32/64 bits) rather than byte-by-byte, which can actually improve performance on some architectures while eliminating timing side channels. The approach focuses on balancing security with performance across different CPU architectures.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/597916/][Supporting Allwinner SoCs]]: Maxime Ripard reports on progress mainlining support for Allwinner system-on-chips (SoCs) used in many low-cost tablets. The article covers the transition from Allwinner's proprietary FEX configuration system to device tree, the development of sunxi-babelfish translator for backward compatibility, and the challenges of bringing multimedia drivers (display, audio, video) to mainline Linux. Allwinner's significant market share in tablets (15%) makes this work particularly important for affordable ARM-based devices.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/597918/][GoboLinux 015]]: After a six-year hiatus, GoboLinux 015 is released, featuring a redesigned Linux filesystem hierarchy that organizes programs under /Programs/ directories rather than the traditional /usr/bin, /usr/lib structure. Key changes include migration from /System/Links to /System/Index, adoption of "root" as super user name, live USB support, and Enlightenment as the default desktop environment. The distribution's unique approach to filesystem organization aims to make package management and system administration more intuitive.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/598372/][Linux gets fix for code-execution flaw (Ars Technica)]]: Linux kernel development article discussing Linux gets fix for code-execution flaw (Ars Technica)
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/597895/][Defeating memory comparison timing oracles (Red Hat Security Blog)]]: Florian Weimer examines timing oracles in memory comparison functions like memcmp() that can allow attackers to extract secret data by measuring execution time differences. The article discusses Red Hat's research into making memcmp() oracle-free by processing data in larger chunks (32/64 bits) rather than byte-by-byte, which can actually improve performance on some architectures while eliminating timing side channels. The approach focuses on balancing security with performance across different CPU architectures.

Allwinner's significant market share in tablets (15%) makes this work particularly important for affordable ARM-based devices.

Key changes include migration from /System/Links to /System/Index, adoption of "root" as super user name, live USB support, and Enlightenment as the default desktop environment. - [[https://lwn.net/Articles/598066/][Balazs: Results of Card Sorting the KDE System Settings]]: Summary of user research card sorting to reorganize KDE's system settings interface, aiming to improve discoverability and navigation based on how users group related configuration options.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/598417/][A CyanogenMod 11.0 M6 test drive]]: Hands-on evaluation of CyanogenMod 11.0 (based on Android 4.4) exploring new privacy controls, Theme Engine improvements, and privacy-centric features like Privacy Browser and Per-App Firewall.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/598460/][Braking CPU hotplug]]: Technical discussion on CPU hotplug race conditions where concurrent online/offline operations could cause kernel deadlocks; solution involves serialization via cpu_hotplug_lock mutex and ensuring proper state machine transitions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/598473/][RFC 7258]]: IETF RFC 7258 describes "Pervasive Surveillance" as a threat to the Internet, documenting consensus that mass surveillance undermines trust and requires technical solutions rather than policy alone.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/598486/][Race detection and more with ThreadSanitizer 2]]: Google's ThreadSanitizer 2 (TSan2) uses shadow memory and happens-before tracking to detect data races and memory errors at runtime, supporting pthreads and OpenMP with minimal slowdown.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/598960/][Venturi: The browser is dead. Long live the browser!]]: Discussion of browser architecture evolution where native apps and web convergence through technologies like WebGL and asm.js; argues modern browsers are becoming universal app platforms.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/599126/][Clasen: Introducing GtkInspector]]: Carlos Garnacho presents GtkInspector, a new debugging tool for GTK+ applications allowing developers to inspect widget hierarchies, modify properties in real-time, and trace signal emissions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/599231/][Taking the Eudyptula Challenge]]: Overview of the Eudyptula Challenge, a series of Linux kernel programming exercises designed to teach low-level kernel development through hands-on tasks of increasing complexity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/599354/][Garrett: The desktop and the developer]]: Matthew Garrett examines how desktop Linux has shifted focus from desktop users to server/cloud workloads, with Red Hat/Intel investments targeting cloud and developers rather than traditional desktop UX.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/599580/][2038 is closer than it seems]]: Technical deep-dive into the Year 2038 problem (signed 32-bit time_t overflow on January 19, 2038), covering affected systems, challenges in fixing time_t (kernel, libc, binary compatibility), and ongoing mitigation efforts like file offset redesign.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/599795/][Tux3 posted for review]]: Introduction to Tux3, a from-scratch Linux filesystem by David Howells with copy-on-write metadata, fast fsck, and variable block sizes targeting both rotational and solid-state storage.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/599811/][A quick look at Qt 5.3]]: Qt 5.3 released with Qt Creator 3.1, improved Qt Quick compiler, Wayland compositor basics, and Qt Location positioning APIs; stabilizing around OpenGL ES requirements.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/599844/][Adobe releases Source Serif font]]: Adobe open-sourced Source Serif Pro, a variable-weight serif typeface designed for screen readability, released under SIL Open Font License for use in projects like LibreOffice.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/599846/][FFmpeg adds support for Magic Lantern raw video]]: FFmpeg added support for Canon Magic Lantern RAW (MLV) video format through a new demuxer, enabling conversion and processing of uncompressed RAW footage from modified Canon DSLRs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/601055/][Accessing Wikipedia offline]]: Technical article covering approaches for offline Wikipedia access including Kiwix (ZIM format), Wikipedia's dumps, and media storage optimization for mobile/embedded devices.
# LWN.org

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642205/][The programming talent myth]]: Jacob Kaplan-Moss argues against the harmful "talent myth" in programming that creates a false dichotomy between "rock star" and "worthless" developers, when in reality programming skills follow a normal distribution with most people being average. He contends this myth prevents people from entering the field, drives diversity issues, and sets unrealistic expectations, advocating instead for recognizing programming as learnable skills where being "average is actually pretty awesome" to address the industry's looming talent shortage.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642166/][Random numbers from CPU execution time jitter]]: Proposes using CPU execution timing variations as an entropy source for random number generation, particularly useful for embedded systems with limited entropy sources. The technique measures jitter from factors like cache behavior and pipeline states, but faces skepticism about whether the entropy is truly unpredictable against sophisticated attackers.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642065/][Garrett: Reducing power consumption on Haswell and Broadwell systems]]: Matthew Garrett investigates why Linux consumes excessive power on modern Intel chipsets, achieving 40% idle power reduction (8.5W to 5W) by enabling power-saving features like Panel Self Refresh and proper SATA link power management. Highlights the need for better integration work between hardware vendors and Linux distributions.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642069/][Pagemap: security fixes vs. ABI compatibility]]: Discusses the conflict between security and ABI stability when the `/proc/pid/pagemap` interface was restricted to root to prevent rowhammer attacks. The solution allows non-root access but returns zero for physical page numbers, using the soft-dirty mechanism instead for legitimate debugging use cases like UndoDB.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/642202/][Tracking actual memory utilization]]: Introduces a new `/proc/kpageidle` interface to track memory usage more accurately than RSS by monitoring which pages are actually accessed. Useful for container resource management, it works with memory control groups to distinguish between allocated memory and actively used memory without disrupting page reclaim.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641790/][Rust Once, Run Everywhere]]: Explores Rust's foreign function interface (FFI) capabilities for calling C libraries with zero overhead while maintaining safety through ownership and borrowing principles. Highlights how Rust can create safer abstractions over existing C APIs without performance penalties.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640302/][Plotting tools for networks, part II]]: Continuation of network diagram tools exploration, covering TikZ (LaTeX-based diagramming with automatic layout algorithms) and NetworkX (Python library for network analysis and visualization). Demonstrates how mathematical networks can be analyzed independently from visual representation, with practical examples including character relationship analysis from "Les Miserables" dataset.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640838/][Adding Requests to the standard library]]: Discussion of whether Python's popular Requests HTTP library should be added to the standard library. Key concerns include security certificate management, rapid update requirements for network security, and the mismatch between Python's slow release cycle and Requests' need for frequent updates. Consensus leans toward keeping it as a separate PyPI package.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641103/][Jython Native Interface (JyNI)]]: Project enabling Jython (Python on JVM) to use Python's C extensions by creating an adaptation layer between Java Native Interface and Python's C API. Main challenges include garbage collection integration, object type unification, and handling C API macros that can't be dynamically switched.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641247/][Taking control of SSDs with LightNVM]]: Kernel subsystem proposal for direct management of open-channel SSDs, bypassing onboard flash translation layers. Provides abstraction layer for kernel to manage NVM devices directly, with initial implementation using round-robin FTL algorithm. Aims to improve performance by allowing kernel-level optimization of data placement and garbage collection.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641275/][The kdbuswreck]]: Analysis of the contentious debate around merging kdbus (kernel D-Bus implementation) into Linux kernel. Main objections focus on capability metadata passing, concerns about extending kernel capabilities meaning, and security implications of transmitting process credentials. Discussion reveals fundamental disagreements about kernel/user-space boundaries and capability-based security models.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641435/][Encryption, the NSA, and the front door]]: Analysis of NSA director's proposal for "split key" encryption systems where government and service providers each hold half of encryption keys. Examines technical challenges including key generation/distribution security, potential for abuse, and impact on free software projects that would need to implement mandatory access mechanisms.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/638636/][Stenberg: The state and rate of HTTP/2 adoption]]: Brief report predicting HTTP/2 adoption rates, forecasting 10-30% usage by end of 2015 and majority adoption by 2016, dependent on major platforms like Facebook and Yahoo implementing the protocol.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630989/][FreeBSD Quarterly Status Report]]: Summary of FreeBSD improvements including enhanced Linux compatibility layer, WINE port improvements, hypervisor support (Xen PVH mode, bhyve AMD support), and new VM image creation tools.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/602753/][LAC'14 video archive]]: Announcement of Linux Audio Conference 2014 video recordings availability, including presentations on audio development topics, available in WebM format via rsync and torrent.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641442/][Sourcegraph: A free code search tool for open source developers (Opensource.com)]]: Sourcegraph is a code search engine that semantically indexes open source code, allowing developers to search by repository, package, or function with linked code navigation. However, it only supports Java, Go, Python, JavaScript, Ruby, and Haskell, notably lacking support for C, C++, and Perl, which limits its utility for many legacy and systems programming projects. The article discusses criticisms about the limited language support and comparisons to other tools like Debian Code Search.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640177/][Atomicity of operations]]: Matt Messier presented Skython, a Python implementation without the Global Interpreter Lock (GIL), at the Python Language Summit. The key discussion centered on whether Python operations on data structures like lists and dicts should be atomic when accessed by multiple threads. Jython and IronPython maintain the same atomicity guarantees as CPython, but Skython sacrifices atomicity for performance by allowing race conditions in concurrent updates. The article highlights the need for formal specification of Python's atomicity guarantees.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640359/][Type hints]]: Guido van Rossum presented PEP 484 for type hints in Python 3.5, using function annotations for static analysis rather than runtime optimization. The proposal includes a typing.py module for standard library support, stub files for C extensions, and plans for future syntax improvements. Static analysis tool developers expressed concerns about semantics, duck typing support, and scope definitions, but generally supported the initiative as a step toward better tooling.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640357/][Obstacles for kdbus]]: The kdbus patch set faced significant opposition during its proposed merge into Linux kernel 4.1. Critics raised concerns about performance, security metadata handling, container compatibility, and complexity. Key objections focused on kdbus exposing kernel internal data structures as ABI and whether it should be a generic IPC mechanism rather than D-Bus-specific. The article documents the heated debate between proponents wanting compatibility with existing D-Bus and opponents advocating for cleaner kernel design.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640113/][Persistent memory support progress]]: Linux 4.1 added support for persistent memory through a new driver that treats it as a block device, with DAX filesystem support enabling direct access. The main limitation is the lack of struct page entries for persistent memory, preventing features like mlock() and direct I/O. The article discusses two approaches: removing struct page usage from kernel APIs (complex and risky) or adding page structures (memory-intensive). Long-term solutions may involve larger-granularity memory tracking structures.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639543/][Load tracking in the scheduler]]: This article explores the Linux kernel's Completely Fair Scheduler (CFS) load tracking mechanisms, explaining how the scheduler estimates process load to ensure fair CPU time allocation. It covers scheduling entities, task groups, time slice calculation, per-entity load tracking metrics, and how these concepts apply to multiprocessor systems. The author highlights ongoing challenges with CPU-frequency invariance and big.LITTLE processor support, providing a comprehensive overview of scheduler load estimation complexities.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640420/][DNF replacing yum]]: Fedora's transition from yum to DNF as the default package manager is examined, detailing the implementation strategy where yum becomes a wrapper script redirecting to DNF with deprecation warnings. The article discusses user concerns about compatibility differences, particularly around the --skip-broken flag behavior, and the philosophical debate about whether DNF should maintain full yum compatibility or establish itself as a distinct tool with different design choices.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639998/][Plotting tools for networks, part I]]: This survey covers tools for creating network diagrams, flowcharts, and graph theory visualizations. It introduces Dia as a GUI-based diagram editor with specialized symbol libraries, and Graphviz as a declarative system using the dot language to generate graphs from text specifications. The article demonstrates how different Graphviz layout engines produce varying visualizations and shows practical applications like analyzing Python code dependencies through automated graph generation.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639988/][Turon: Fearless Concurrency with Rust]]: Aaron Turon's article explains Rust's approach to thread safety through compile-time ownership and borrowing checks that prevent data races without runtime overhead. The language's type system ensures thread safety by tracking whether data types can be safely sent between or accessed by multiple threads. The discussion covers practical examples of parallel matrix computation and addresses questions about Rust's suitability for kernel programming and scientific computing.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640111/][Hubička: Link time and inter-procedural optimization improvements in GCC 5]]: Jan Hubička details significant optimization enhancements in GCC 5, including new identical code folding that eliminates duplicate functions from template instantiations, improved link-time optimization (LTO) with better whole-program analysis, and enhanced inter-procedural optimization (IPA) capabilities. The improvements result in smaller binaries and better performance through more aggressive dead code elimination and cross-module optimization.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640198/][The Document Liberation, one year after]]: The Document Liberation Project provides libraries for handling proprietary document formats within LibreOffice, with progress including new framework libraries and support for formats like Adobe PageMaker, Microsoft Works, and legacy Mac formats, enabling easier integration for other software projects.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/640316/][The GNU Make Book -- New from No Starch Press]]: No Starch Press released "The GNU Make Book" covering GNU Make basics and advanced topics like build optimization and parallelization, providing developers with comprehensive guidance on this essential build automation tool.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639072/][A different approach to application containers with Limba]]: Limba offers an alternative to xdg-app with dynamic runtime dependencies instead of static runtimes, using AppStream metadata and OverlayFS for application isolation while relying on upstream ABI stability rather than fixed runtime environments.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639258/][Realtime using the PRU]]: ARM SoCs' Programmable Realtime Unit (PRU) provides deterministic realtime capabilities with dedicated 200MHz RISC cores and fast I/O, enabling 5ns GPIO transitions for drone control and other time-critical tasks while Linux handles general processing.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639427/][Ext4 encryption]]: Ext4 now includes native per-directory encryption using AES-256 with per-file keys, reducing memory usage compared to stacked filesystems and enabling selective encryption for Android/Chrome OS use cases where full-disk encryption is impractical.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639333/][Running the kernel in library mode]]: Introduces LibOS, a patch set that enables running the Linux kernel as a shared library in user space, primarily focused on making the kernel's network stack available to applications for use cases like user-space networking (NUSE) and network simulation (NS-3), while addressing maintenance concerns about keeping stub functions synchronized with kernel changes.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/638722/][Write-stream IDs]]: Proposes adding 8-bit write-stream identifiers to block I/O operations to help SSDs and other large-block devices reduce write amplification by grouping data with similar lifetimes, with the ID stored in both file and inode structures to support both direct and buffered I/O scenarios.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/638908/][An update on the freedreno graphics driver]]: Provides status report on the open-source freedreno driver for Qualcomm Adreno GPUs, covering support for Adreno 2xx/3xx/4xx series, reverse engineering progress, Gallium driver architecture, and ongoing work on OpenGL ES 3.0 features like transform feedback and uniform buffer objects.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639000/][What to Expect When You're Expecting: PHP 7, Part 1 (Engine Yard)]]: Highlights new features in PHP 7 including the "spaceship operator" (<=>) for three-way comparisons returning -1/0/1 values, scalar type hints for better type checking, and an AST (Abstract Syntax Tree) for improved parsing and compilation.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/639616/][Teach Your Kids to Code -- New from No Starch Press]]: Announces a new book designed to help parents and educators teach Python programming to children through game-oriented examples using Turtle graphics, covering basic syntax, loops, lists, functions, and building games like War, Yahtzee, and Pong.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/601823/][Kuhn: Why your project doesn't need a contributor licensing agreement]]: Bradley Kuhn argues that free software projects don't need contributor license agreements (CLAs) - clear statements that contributions are offered under the project's license are sufficient. The article discusses the controversy around FSF's copyright assignment requirements and legal complexities in non-US jurisdictions.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/601243/][Anonymous, wireless file sharing with PirateBox]]: Describes PirateBox, a portable WiFi server based on OpenWrt that creates anonymous local file-sharing networks without internet connectivity. Uses TP-Link routers to provide chat, message boards, and media streaming for local collaboration at events, meetings, or remote locations.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/601428/][Day: Notify me]]: Covers GNOME 3's notification system redesign by Allan Day, aiming to balance visibility with distraction-free experience. The article discusses user feedback about notification discoverability issues and philosophical debates about GNOME's design principles regarding window management and user workflow.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/601692/][Prodromou: The future of pump.io]]: Evan Prodromou discusses development plans for pump.io, the federated social networking platform, as he transitions from full-time work. Focuses on reducing administrative overhead for public servers and addressing pull requests and issues for upcoming 0.4 release.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/601799/][The BFQ I/O scheduler]]: Jonathan Corbet explains the Budget Fair Queuing I/O scheduler that improves on CFQ by assigning per-process I/O budgets based on weight and behavior. BFQ reduces latencies through sophisticated heuristics for application startup, device characteristics, and real-time workloads, with detailed documentation of its algorithms.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641197/][The Puppet design philosophy (O'Reilly)]]: O'Reilly excerpt explaining Puppet's declarative configuration management approach, contrasting with procedural scripting. Highlights challenges of immutable resource definitions and variable assignments that require upfront planning, with community discussion about workarounds and comparisons to Chef's Ruby-based approach.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/641442/][Sourcegraph: A free code search tool for open source developers (Opensource.com)]]: Introduction to Sourcegraph's semantic code indexing for open source projects, supporting Java, Go, Python, JavaScript, Ruby, and Haskell. Criticized for lacking support for C, C++, and Perl, limiting utility for systems programming. Community discussion compares it to Debian Code Search and highlights limitations for legacy codebases.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/637037/][Conflict over a code]]: Analysis of the Linux kernel's newly adopted "code of conflict" addressing behavioral issues in the development community. The article examines differing interpretations of the document - from being seen as an attempt to rein in Linus Torvalds to being viewed as an ineffective no-op statement.
