The code emphasizes that technical conflict is normal but personal abuse is not, though it lacks specific prohibited behaviors or sanctions, placing resolution responsibility on the Technical Advisory Board.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/637151/][Filesystem fuzzing]]: Sasha Levin's Vault 2015 presentation on filesystem fuzzing techniques for kernel testing. Covers structure fuzzing (modifying filesystem images) and API fuzzing (passing random parameters to system calls), highlighting bugs like CVE-2015-1420 found through smart fuzzing that understands parameter types and concurrency patterns. Discusses challenges like reproducing bugs and the need for continuous fuzzing.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636730/][Virtual filesystem layer changes, past and future]]: Al Viro's LSFMM 2015 update on VFS evolution, covering the transition to iov_iter interface for I/O operations, challenges with FUSE and splice() zero-copy I/O, and the new fs_pin mechanism for clean filesystem unmounting. Also discusses making nameidata structure opaque and removing BSD process accounting's problematic unmount behavior.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636288/][Filesystem/block interfaces]]: Steven Whitehouse's LSFMM 2015 discussion on improving communication between filesystem and block layers for dynamic devices, innovative I/O (SMR, persistent memory), and snapshots. Highlights the need for better error reporting distinguishing transient vs permanent errors and callback mechanisms for filesystems to respond to block layer changes.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636943/][Overlayfs issues and experiences]]: David Howells and Mike Snitzer's LSFMM 2015 session on overlayfs problems including file locking, fanotify, and SELinux label visibility across layers. Discusses Docker's adoption of overlayfs for memory efficiency and the challenge of page cache deduplication between containers sharing the same base filesystem.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636967/][Asynchronous buffered read operations]]: Milosz Tanski's LSFMM 2015 proposal for preadv2() system call with RWF_NONBLOCK flag that allows applications to avoid thread pools by distinguishing between page cache hits (fast) and disk I/O (slow). The flag returns EAGAIN if data isn't cached, enabling more efficient I/O multiplexing and showing 23% latency improvements in testing.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636978/][Handling 32KB-block drives]]: Discussion at LSFMM 2015 about supporting 32KB sector drives despite the Linux page cache's 4KB granularity. Filesystems could use read-modify-write operations and alignment tricks, but drive manufacturers should provide emulation like they did for 4KB sectors. The fundamental mismatch between page size and block size suggests drive-level solutions are preferable to kernel modifications.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/637035/][Filesystem support for SMR devices]]: Exploration of shingled magnetic recording (SMR) drive support challenges at LSFMM 2015. Host-managed SMR requires sequential writes to specific zones, creating ordering dependencies that conflict with filesystem allocation patterns. The "write allocate" command proposal would let drives choose block locations, potentially solving the sequential write requirement while maintaining filesystem compatibility.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/637079/][Testing power failures]]: Josef Bacik's LSFMM 2015 presentation on a device-mapper-based tool for reproducing filesystem corruption during power failures. The tool logs write operations to a secondary disk and replays them to test consistency after simulated crashes. Unlike fault injection, this approach preserves write ordering and enables systematic testing of rare corruption scenarios across ext4, XFS, and Btrfs.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636797/][Reservations for must-succeed memory allocations]]: LSFMM 2015 discussion on memory reservation systems for allocations that cannot fail (like XFS transactions). The proposed solution involves pre-allocating worst-case memory estimates before critical operations, using a GFP flag to access reserves when needed. This addresses deadlock risks in low-memory scenarios where the OOM killer cannot make progress due to lock dependencies.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636301/][Heterogeneous memory management]]: Jérôme Glisse's LSFMM 2015 presentation on HMM for sharing memory between CPUs and GPUs on the same die. HMM enables memory migration between devices while maintaining page table synchronization through MMU notifiers. The system treats GPU memory like a swap file and handles atomic access via read-only mappings, though challenges remain with file-backed pages requiring non-atomic filesystem operations.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636331/][Current issues with memory control groups]]: LSFMM 2015 discussion on remaining memcg challenges after Vladimir Davydov's kernel memory tracking improvements. Key topics include whether separate kernel-space memory limits are needed versus combined user/kernel limits, applying Unix-style resource limits to control groups, and tracking page table memory usage as the next development priority.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636334/][Memory-management scalability]]: LSFMM 2015 discussion on VM scalability challenges with growing core counts and memory sizes. Topics include moving beyond per-CPU variables to NUMA-aware data structures, mmap_sem contention issues, range locking proposals for address space concurrency, and the ongoing effort to document what mmap_sem actually protects before implementing finer-grained locking.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636549/][Memory-management testing and debugging]]: LSFMM 2015 overview of testing and debugging tools including mmtests integration, Intel MPX for hardware-based memory safety, VM_BUG_ON improvements, KASan enhancements for vmalloc() and quarantine features, and the proposal to remove the obsolete kmemcheck utility in favor of more modern debugging approaches.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636972/][Improving page reclaim]]: LSFMM 2015 discussion on adapting page reclaim algorithms for persistent memory devices that require lower overhead than traditional swap. Proposals include adding a third LRU level for swap-ready pages, batching operations for fast random-access devices, and questioning whether 4KB page granularity remains appropriate for large-capacity nonvolatile memory systems.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636973/][Huge pages and persistent memory]]: Matthew Wilcox's LSFMM 2015 presentation on DAX huge page support challenges, including the pmd_special() function for tracking persistent memory mappings without page structures. Discussion covers copy-on-write behavior for huge pages, kernel mapping interfaces for persistent memory, and proposals for a level-independent page table abstraction to reduce code duplication.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/637080/][Investigating a performance bottleneck]]: LSFMM 2015 discussion on NFS performance issues with low-latency transports. Chuck Lever identified wake_up_bit() contention causing 300µs RPC delays during client loads, with debugging suggestions including latency tracer usage, IPI timing analysis, and power management effects on processor states.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/637195/][KDE and The Semantic Desktop]]: Vishesh Handa's retrospective on KDE's semantic desktop evolution from RDF-based Nepomuk to the simpler Baloo file indexing system. The transition addressed limitations of centralized RDF stores while maintaining search functionality without the semantic complexity that proved difficult for application integration.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/635771/][Progress in security module stacking]]: Coverage of Casey Schaufler's LSM stacking patches (v21) that enable multiple security modules to run simultaneously by replacing security_operations with security_list_options. The simplified approach avoids monolithic LSM conflicts while supporting single-purpose modules like Yama alongside capabilities and one primary security model.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636136/][Exploiting the DRAM rowhammer bug to gain kernel privileges]]: Google Project Zero's demonstration of DRAM rowhammer vulnerability exploitation through repeated memory row access causing bit flips in adjacent rows. The attack induces page table entry corruption to gain kernel privileges, with mitigations requiring memory controller refresh rate adjustments or ECC memory protection.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636096/][Progress on persistent memory]]: Matthew Wilcox's LSFMM 2015 update on persistent memory support challenges including struct page overhead for large devices, new Intel instructions (clflushopt, clwb, pcommit), and error handling strategies for memory-mapped persistent storage requiring filesystem coordination with bad block reporting.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636017/][Allowing small allocations to fail]]: Michal Hocko's LSFMM 2015 proposal to disable the kernel's "too small to fail" behavior where order-3 (8-page) allocations retry indefinitely. The plan introduces a sysctl knob for gradual transition from indefinite retries to immediate failures, addressing issues with OOM killer unpredictability and system lockups.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636162/][Improving huge page handling]]: LSFMM 2015 discussions on transparent huge page improvements including Kirill Shutemov's reference counting patches for simultaneous PMD/PTE mappings and Hugh Dickins' tmpfs implementation avoiding compound pages. Vlastimil Babka proposed moving page scanning to process context to reduce compaction latency during page faults.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636226/][User-space page fault handling]]: Andrea Arcangeli's userfaultfd() patch enabling user-space page fault handling for KVM live migration and CRIU container checkpointing. The mechanism allows blocking page faults while a user-space monitor process resolves missing pages, supporting both same-process and cross-process monitoring scenarios.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636234/][Fixing the contiguous memory allocator]]: LSFMM 2015 sessions on CMA problems including pinned pages blocking large allocations and underutilization of reserved memory. Solutions discussed include immediate migration of pinned pages and Joonsoo Kim's ZONE_CMA proposal for better allocation policies and statistics.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/636129/][Building HTTP/2 services with gRPC]]: Google's new RPC framework leveraging HTTP/2 features like bidirectional streaming and multiplexing with protocol buffers serialization. The service definition language generates client/server stubs in multiple languages, providing performance improvements over HTTP 1.1 REST APIs.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/635513/][A first look at the CANBus Triple]]: Review of an open-hardware CAN bus device with three independent channels, ATMEGA 32u4 microcontroller, and USB/Bluetooth connectivity for automotive hacking. The device bridges the gap between basic Arduino CAN shields and expensive USB adapters, enabling CAN message interception and modification for aftermarket automotive applications.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/635354/][Memory management when failure is not an option]]: Analysis of kernel memory allocation challenges when GFP_NOFAIL flags are required, particularly for filesystem transactions. Discusses conflicts between memory management developers wanting allocation failure handling and filesystem developers needing guaranteed memory for complex operations, with proposals for reservation systems to prevent deadlocks.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/635222/][A look at EasyNAS]]: Review of a Btrfs-based NAS distribution built on openSUSE, featuring web administration interface for storage management and snapshot functionality. The project lacks advanced features like plugin support, LDAP integration, and comprehensive resource monitoring compared to alternatives like Rockstor and FreeNAS.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/635009/][The state of Linux gaming in the SteamOS era (Ars Technica)]]: Overview of Linux gaming progress with SteamOS, noting increased native game availability but ongoing challenges with 32-bit binary compatibility and Valve's slow development timeline. The article discusses how Steam has created a viable Linux gaming market despite platform fragmentation issues.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/634674/][Building GNOME Builder]]: Christian Hergert's SCALE 13x presentation on the GNOME IDE project designed to lower barriers for new developers through integrated tutorials and GNOME-specific tooling. Builder uses Clang for live diagnostics, supports multiple build systems and VCS, and aims to simplify D-Bus integration and cross-compilation for embedded development.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/634452/][Makers and open source]]: Analysis of the maker movement's relationship with open source principles, highlighting concerns about the trend toward "open by accident" rather than intentional sharing. Discusses how open source communities can help makers address challenges like cloning, legal issues, and sustainable business models that the software world has already solved.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/634262/][Green: Another update on the Truecrypt audit]]: Update on the TrueCrypt audit project led by Matthew Green, which contracted with NCC Group's Cryptography Services to evaluate TrueCrypt 7.1a as a baseline for newer forks. The audit aims to assess the security of the encryption tool despite its abrupt shutdown in 2014.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/634803/][Lazytime hits a snag]]: Report on issues with the lazytime feature in Linux 4.0 that delays writing file access times to improve performance. Jan Kara identified problems causing incorrect time recording, potentially requiring the feature to be disabled in the initial 4.0 release until fixes are implemented.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/634649/][A rough patch for live patching]]: Coverage of challenges in developing a unified consistency model for Linux kernel live patching, with debates over stack-trace reliability and alternative approaches. Ingo Molnar proposed rethinking the entire concept in favor of full-system checkpoint/restore for kernel upgrades.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/634777/][Key management with Gentoo Keys]]: Introduction to Gentoo's new Python toolkit for handling OpenPGP keys according to GLEP 63 guidelines. The gkeys utility manages key distribution, validation, and signature verification for Gentoo's release media, packages, and developer-signed documents.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/634488/][A GNU C Library update]]: Covers glibc 2.20 and 2.21 releases featuring Intel MPX support, lock elision for s390, optimized ARM string functions, and removal of deprecated feature test macros. Future plans include improved testing infrastructure, better benchmarks, and support for more architectures.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/634487/][Morevna Production Report #1]]: Reports on the Morevna Project's anime production using Synfig Studio, focusing on bug fixes and stability improvements for the upcoming stable release. The project uses free software tools to create anime videos based on Russian folk tales.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/633835/][A look at LibreOffice 4.4]]: Discusses LibreOffice 4.4's UI/UX improvements including GtkBuilder dialog boxes, reorganized toolbars, and enhanced sidebar functionality. Also covers new file format support, improved Microsoft Office compatibility, and code quality improvements from fixing 6,000+ Coverity scan defects.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/633203/][Scalar typing in the PHP world]]: Covers the contentious debate around adding strict scalar type hints to PHP 7, including the compromise proposal using declare(strict_types=1) to let calling code decide whether to enforce strict type checking. The feature aims to improve error detection while preserving PHP's flexible typing heritage.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/633422/][Epoll evolving]]: Describes new epoll system call proposals including epoll_ctl_batch() for multi-descriptor operations and EPOLLEXCLUSIVE/EPOLLROUNDROBIN flags for better multi-threaded performance by avoiding thundering herd wakeups when multiple threads poll the same descriptors.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/633538/][Creating scalable APIs]]: Explores the "scalable commutativity rule" for designing parallel software APIs that avoid scalability bottlenecks on multicore systems. Covers SIM commutativity analysis tools and implementation techniques like embracing non-determinism, deferring work, and optimistic execution to improve multicore performance.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/633273/][Reproducible Android app builds]]: Describes F-Droid and Guardian Project's efforts to create deterministic Android app builds that produce bit-for-bit identical APK files from source code. This allows verification that distributed binaries match published source, enhancing security and trust in mobile applications.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/633153/][Linux for Astronomers (Linux Journal)]]: Overview of Distro Astro, a Linux distribution tailored for astronomy work with specialized tools for telescope control, image capture, astrophotography, and celestial observation management using free software applications.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/633907/][Routing on OpenStreetMap.org]]: Announces OpenStreetMap's new routing feature that provides point-to-point directions directly on the main site. This encourages users to improve map data quality by fixing routing-related issues like turn restrictions and path connectivity problems.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/632773/][Emacs and LLDB]]: Covers the debate around adding LLDB debugger support to Emacs' Grand Unified Debugger mode, including Richard Stallman's concerns about LLVM/LLDB's BSD license and its relationship to GNU toolchain development.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/632572/][Matrix: a new specification for federated realtime chat]]: Introduces the Matrix protocol for decentralized real-time communication using HTTP/JSON with persistent message history synchronization across federated servers. Features include IRC-like rooms with decentralized access control, support for multiple simultaneous clients, and eventual consistency via cryptographically signed event DAGs, though end-to-end encryption was still in development.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/632914/][Stem 1.3 makes hidden services easier to deploy]]: Covers the Tor project's Python library update that simplifies hidden service deployment with new methods like create_hidden_service() and remove_hidden_service() for programmatic management. The release also includes 40% faster directory authority parsing and improved connection statistics, making it easier to run Tor-based services like web servers or SSH servers through .onion addresses.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/632520/][Inheriting capabilities]]: Discusses Christoph Lameter's patch for Linux capability inheritance across execve() calls, addressing a fundamental limitation where processes cannot pass privileges to child programs. The proposal introduces an "ambient capability set" that allows controlled privilege inheritance for use cases like user-space network stacks that need to spawn helper programs with limited root privileges.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/632528/][The bootstrap process on EFI systems]]: Comprehensive guide to Linux boot methods on UEFI platforms, covering legacy EFI boot using loaders like GRUB, the EFI boot stub (CONFIG_EFI_STUB) that embeds boot code in the kernel, and the EFI handover protocol that combines loader features with early kernel workarounds for firmware bugs.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/632118/][GCC5 and the C++11 ABI (Red Hat developer blog)]]: Explains GCC 5's C++11 ABI changes for std::string and std::list that require different symbol mangling to avoid soname bumps. The solution uses namespace-based name mangling to allow both old and new ABIs to coexist in libstdc++ while maintaining binary compatibility.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631827/][A test run of openHAB 1.6]]: Technical review of openHAB 1.6, a Java-based home automation system using OSGi component model. The article evaluates device support for 99 protocols, configuration complexity with sitemap files, and the web/Android/iOS interfaces. Discusses advantages of bus-based architecture over monolithic systems and compares it to competitors like Home Assistant and MisterHouse.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631325/][A look at Inkscape 0.91]]: Comprehensive review of Inkscape 0.91 vector graphics editor after 4+ years of development. Covers new features including measuring tool, PowerStroke pen, improved alignment tools, radial arrangement, gradient/text enhancements, and performance improvements with Cairo rendering and OpenMP. Discusses the roadmap toward SVG 1.1 compliance for version 1.0.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631853/][Linux as a single-user system]]: Analysis of kernel patch proposing single-user mode for embedded systems to save memory (~25KB). The patch removes multi-user support, running all processes as root and eliminating user/group ID system calls. Discusses debate over whether this violates "Linux behavior" principles and compares to historical authoritative LSM hooks proposal.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631509/][Statistics from the 3.19 development cycle]]: Detailed statistics for Linux kernel 3.19 development with 12,461 changesets from 1,422 developers. Top contributors include Hartley Sweeten (Comedi drivers) and Malcolm Priestley (staging drivers). Analysis shows Intel, Red Hat, and independent developers as major contributors, with code longevity trends showing most kernel code remains unchanged for years.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631631/][How programs get run: ELF binaries]]: Technical deep dive into Linux ELF binary execution, covering format structure, program header processing, memory mapping, stack setup with auxiliary vector, and dynamic linking. Explains the complete execve() process from kernel perspective including credential handling, signal setup, and compatibility support for 32-bit/x32 binaries.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631216/][FreeNAS — network-attached storage with ZFS]]: Review of FreeNAS 9.3, a FreeBSD-based NAS distribution featuring ZFS filesystem with RAID support, snapshotting, deduplication, and encryption. The article compares it to Linux-based alternatives, noting its maturity but higher memory requirements (8GB minimum recommended) and slower boot times.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631888/][You're the Boss with UBOS (Linux Journal)]]: Overview of UBOS, a Linux distribution designed for easy home server setup with support for ownCloud, WordPress, MediaWiki and other applications. The beta version runs on PCs, Raspberry Pi, and VirtualBox, aiming to make server administration accessible to non-experts.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631475/][Plotting tools for Linux: matplotlib]]: Comprehensive guide to matplotlib, a Python library for scientific plotting that integrates with NumPy and SciPy. Covers installation, basic plotting with pyplot interface, 3D visualization with mplot3d, LaTeX integration for publication-quality labels, and PGF export for embedding in LaTeX documents.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/631879/][No Starch Press and Humble Bundle Present the Brainiac Book Bundle]]: Announcement of a pay-what-you-want ebook bundle featuring programming and STEM education books for children, including titles on Python, JavaScript, HTML/CSS, LEGO building, and computer science concepts. Proceeds support EFF and Freedom of the Press Foundation.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630778/][Matthew Garrett versus IPMI]]: Security analysis of Intelligent Platform Management Interface (IPMI) implementations, highlighting vulnerabilities in BMC firmware including command injection, XML parser flaws, and authentication weaknesses. Discusses the challenges of securing these out-of-band management systems and recommends network segregation and updates.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630542/][Writing Linux Test Project test cases]]: Comprehensive guide to writing LTP test cases using the LTP test library, which provides safe macros for POSIX interfaces, automatic cleanup, and result reporting. Covers test structure with setup()/cleanup() functions, safe file operations, block device handling, and parent-child synchronization for testing system call behavior and error conditions.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630805/][Pettycoin and sidechaining]]: Analysis of Rusty Russell's Pettycoin project, a Bitcoin sidechain concept for microtransactions with 10-second block times versus Bitcoin's 10 minutes. Discusses how sidechains enable bi-directional gateways to Bitcoin while allowing different transaction rules, and how the 2014 sidechains paper influenced Pettycoin's design for partial-knowledge clients and miner payment mechanisms.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630866/][An overhyped GHOST]]: Critical examination of the GHOST glibc vulnerability (CVE-2015-0235), a heap buffer overflow in gethostbyname() functions that was fixed in 2013 but not recognized as security-critical. The article discusses the difficulty of exploitation, the role of PR firms in vulnerability disclosure, and the actual impact being limited primarily to Exim mail servers with non-default configurations.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630762/][A crypto module loading vulnerability]]: Description of CVE-2013-7421, a kernel vulnerability where unprivileged users could load arbitrary kernel modules via AF_ALG crypto sockets. The fix involved adding "crypto-" prefixes to module aliases, similar to the "fs-" prefix fix for mount vulnerabilities. The article also covers the related BusyBox modprobe bug (CVE-2014-9645) that bypassed the security mechanism.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630727/][How programs get run]]: First part of a technical deep dive into Linux program execution, covering the execve() system call implementation including linux_binprm structure setup, binary format handler iteration, and script interpretation. Explains how the kernel processes #! scripts by modifying argument lists and recursively invoking interpreters, with comparisons to binfmt_misc for dynamic format support.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630387/][A two-part series on LXC networking]]: Flockport Labs' comprehensive guide covering LXC networking concepts and practical container connectivity. Part 1 introduces LXC networking basics and extending layer 2 to remote hosts using layer 3 tunnels, while Part 2 explores using LXC containers as routers with Ethernet over GRE and L2tpv3 protocols for layer 2 network extension.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630546/][New open source dependency manager on the scene]]: Introduction to biicode, an open-source dependency management system for C/C++ applications similar to Ruby Gems or Python Package Index. The project transitioned from proprietary to open source, aiming to solve C/C++ library management challenges across different platforms including Windows compatibility issues and file-based dependency resolution.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629580/][The democratization of radio]]: David Rowe's linux.conf.au talk on software-defined radio (SDR) evolution, where open-source software is replacing proprietary hardware components in radio systems. Discusses case studies including Mesh Potato VOIP routers, echo cancellation software, and FreeDV HF radio, highlighting the advantages of open development for radio communications technology.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630018/][Drones running (and compiling) Linux]]: Andrew Tridgell's demonstration of Linux-based UAV autopilot systems using BeagleBone Black with PixHawk cape. Shows real-time sensor processing with 1200 SPI transactions per second, six realtime threads for navigation, and the growth of Linux-based drone projects including Erle Brain, navIO, and the Dronecode collaborative project.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629714/][A verifiable source of random numbers]]: Jim Cheetham and Paul Campbell present OneRNG, a hardware random number generator using avalanche diode quantum noise and optional RF receiver entropy. Features open-source verification of all components including firmware, schematics, and whitening functions, designed to provide trustworthy entropy for cryptography and other applications requiring high-quality randomness.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630115/][Dropping x86 EISA support]]: Discussion of Paul Gortmaker's proposal to remove EISA bus support from 32-bit x86 kernels, which was blocked when Maciej W. Rozycki confirmed active use for EISA FDDI equipment. Highlights the ongoing tension between cleaning legacy code and maintaining compatibility for specialized hardware users in the Linux kernel community.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629742/][When real validation begins]]: Paul McKenney's LCA 2015 talk on challenges with full dynamic tick support in RHEL7 kernel, where RCU callback offloading caused 40% CPU usage on systems with high context switching. Details the iterative debugging process and lessons about testing assumptions across diverse workloads.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629965/][Inserting a hole into a file]]: Namjae Jeon's FALLOC_FL_INSERT_RANGE proposal for fallocate() system call, allowing block-aligned hole insertion in files without data copying. Useful for video editing and scientific applications, implemented for XFS and extent-based ext4 filesystems with similar constraints to the existing FALLOC_FL_COLLAPSE_RANGE.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630216/][GNOME and application sandboxing revisited]]: GNOME's renewed effort on desktop application containers using xdg-app tool, with per-user/system-wide installations, Kdbus IPC, and Wayland display. Based on GNOME 3.15 runtime with control groups, namespaces, and SELinux sandboxing to enable cross-distribution application deployment.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630249/][GNU coreutils 2014 update]]: Pádraig Brady's summary of coreutils development including new dd status=progress option, chroot improvements, and multi-call binary support. Highlights both accepted changes and rejected proposals for various command-line utilities.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/630234/][Meeks: LibreOffice Android View (Beta)]]: Michael Meeks announces LibreOffice file viewer for Android with initial writer functionality providing good document viewing, basic spreadsheet and presentation support. Available on Google Play Store as beta software with known bugs left intentionally for community contribution.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629871/][Taylor: gnome-battery-bench]]: Owen Taylor introduces power measurement tool for Linux systems to extend battery life, providing graphical feedback on power usage and estimated battery life. Features both GUI for interactive exploration and command-line version for automated scripting, using recorded event sequences for accurate user interaction simulation.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629259/][Extracting the abstract syntax tree from GCC]]: Debate between Richard Stallman and developers over exporting GCC's AST to Emacs for IDE features. Stallman fears proprietary backends could misuse AST information, while developers argue LLVM/clang already provide similar capabilities and GCC risks losing developer mindshare without modern IDE integration.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629286/][Software-defined radio at the OpenRadio miniconf]]: LCA 2015 miniconf covering free software and amateur radio with SDR focus. Featured OpenRadio hardware kit construction - Arduino-controlled SDR transceiver on 27MHz ISM band with prototyping area for frequency filters. Demonstrates Quisk and fldigi software for signal demodulation.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629155/][Improving Linux networking performance]]: Jesper Brouer's work optimizing Linux networking for 100Gb/s speeds, focusing on batching operations to reduce per-packet overhead. Discusses cache miss costs, locking overhead, and memory management challenges, with qmempool prototype showing 40ns improvements in packet forwarding tests.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629152/][Toward a more efficient slab allocator]]: Christoph Lameter's LCA 2015 talk on improving Linux slab allocator performance with batch allocation API (kmem_cache_alloc_array) and fragmentation reduction techniques. Covers per-CPU allocation, partial page sorting, off-node allocation, and future movable object support to address slab page fragmentation issues.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628705/][Rockstor — A Btrfs-based NAS distribution]]: Jonathan Corbet reviews Rockstor, a CentOS-based NAS distribution using Btrfs filesystem with web management interface. Features Btrfs snapshots, replication, and pool management but notes immature implementation with USB boot issues and incomplete CLI tools in early 2015 release.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/629362/][Android gets a toybox]]: Jake Edge reports on toybox BSD-licensed command-line utility collection replacing Android's toolbox, similar to BusyBox but avoiding GPL licensing concerns. Google's Android team adopts toybox for improved GNU compatibility and familiar Linux utility behavior in embedded systems.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627345/][Some unreliable predictions for 2015]]: Jonathan Corbet's annual predictions including IoT Linux competition, systemd wars winding down, more Heartbleed-level security incidents, year-2038 problem progress, and Btrfs/Wayland/Python3 traction. Notes ongoing community civility discussions and LWN's 17th year of publication.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628621/][Dark Mail publishes its secure-email architecture]]: Nathan Willis covers Dark Internet Mail Environment (DIME) specification by Lavabit and Silent Circle founders. Describes encrypted metadata, separate field encryption with multiple keys, domain-based authentication via DNS and keyservers, and federated identity management to prevent government surveillance.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628537/][Plotting tools for Linux: gnuplot]]: Comprehensive overview of gnuplot, a versatile command-line plotting program for Linux that supports 2D/3D graphs, data analysis, LaTeX integration, and multiple output formats. The article covers installation, basic usage examples including Bessel functions and 3D surface plots, data fitting capabilities, and integration with LaTeX for publication-quality graphics.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628343/][Docker image "verification"]]: Critical analysis revealing Docker's image verification feature is misleading - it only checks for a signed manifest but doesn't verify image contents, allowing attackers to substitute malicious images. The article details security vulnerabilities including unverified xz decompression running as root, TarSum hashing flaws, and unpacking vulnerabilities before verification.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628207/][The Darkmail Internet Mail Environment]]: Introduction to DIME, a secure email protocol designed by Phillip Zimmermann and Ladar Levison to replace SMTP with multi-layer encryption and key management. The specification aims to limit metadata disclosure by ensuring handling agents only access necessary information through layered encryption and key management systems.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628531/][Haunted by ancient history]]: Discussion of kernel development's no-regressions policy through two recent examples: wireless extensions API removal (reverted due to wicd network manager and scripts dependency) and ARM bogomips removal (reverted after breaking pyaudio). Shows the challenge of maintaining backward compatibility while modernizing kernel interfaces.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628628/][The problem with nested sleeping primitives]]: Analysis of race conditions when kernel code nests sleeping primitives within wait condition checks. The article explains how new wait_woken() API with WQ_FLAG_WOKEN flag solves the problem by safely handling wakeups between condition checks and schedule() calls, preventing infinite waits.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628284/][OpenMediaVault: a distribution for NAS boxes]]: Review of OpenMediaVault, a Debian-based network-attached storage distribution featuring web-based administration, disk management, RAID support, and network file sharing services. The article covers installation requirements (full disk allocation), PHP-based admin interface, and plugin system for extending functionality beyond basic file serving.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628548/][Cuthbertson: NixOS and Stateless Deployment]]: Analysis of NixOS advantages over traditional configuration management tools like Puppet, emphasizing its declarative, exhaustive approach where unspecified system components are absent rather than left alone. The article discusses NixOS's immutable package management and stateless deployment model for reproducible server configurations.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628743/][The building blocks of a distribution with Linux from Scratch (Opensource.com)]]: Overview of Linux from Scratch (LFS) methodology for building custom Linux distributions from source code, with variants supporting both sysvinit and systemd init systems. The article explains how LFS provides a minimal base system that can be extended through the Beyond Linux from Scratch collection.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628527/][An "open governance" fork of Node.js]]: Coverage of the io.js fork created by Node.js developers dissatisfied with Joyent's governance model, focusing on faster release cycles and open technical committee decision-making. The article examines the fork's compatibility goals, governance structure, and potential impact on the Node.js ecosystem.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/628486/][GIMP 2014 report]]: Summary of GIMP's 2014 development progress including text tool improvements with HarfBuzz integration for complex writing systems, 64-bit per channel color precision support, and performance enhancements through GEGL's multi-threading and OpenCL acceleration for resource-intensive image processing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627341/][And so ends another year...]]: Jonathan Corbet's year-end review reflecting on 2014 predictions including ARM servers, surveillance awareness, patent trolls, systemd adoption, Btrfs progress, and challenges facing LWN with comment quality issues, with a personal note about health recovery.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627230/][Monkeysign 2.0]]: Monkeysign 2.0 release - a Python-based OpenPGP key signing tool using QR codes for fingerprint exchange and email for signature delivery, aiming to make PGP key signing easier at key-signing parties.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627600/][Live kernel patching on track for 3.20]]: Jiri Kosina announced unified live kernel patching infrastructure merging kpatch and kgraft approaches, targeting inclusion in Linux 3.20 kernel.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627232/][CoreOS looks to move from Btrfs to overlayfs]]: CoreOS planning to switch from Btrfs to ext4+overlayfs due to Btrfs issues with out-of-space errors, metadata rebalancing, and performance; Red Hat evaluation shows overlayfs is faster for Docker containers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627419/][The "too small to fail" memory-allocation rule]]: Discussion of kernel's unwritten rule that small GFP_KERNEL allocations never fail, leading to OOM killer deadlocks when processes holding locks need memory to exit.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627431/][Devuan progress report]]: Devuan (Debian fork without systemd) reports progress on build infrastructure with continuous integration and first package built through GitLab.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627482/][Prokop: Ten years of Grml]]: Michael Prokop reflects on Grml's ten years of development including migrations from Subversion to Mercurial to Git, and sub-projects like grml-zshrc and jenkins-debian-glue.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626866/][Klapper: Good bye Bugzilla, welcome Phabricator]]: Wikimedia's migration from Bugzilla to Phabricator after 10 years and 70,000+ bugs, including details on data migration challenges.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627095/][Tagged memory and minion cores in the lowRISC SoC]]: lowRISC project plans tagged memory for fine-grained security and minion cores for I/O processing in their RISC-V based open-source SoC.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627610/][Kuhn: Toward Civil Behavior]]: Bradley Kuhn discusses abusive behavior in FLOSS communities and the need for civil conduct standards.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627341/][And so ends another year...]]: LWN's year-end retrospective on 2014 predictions; ARM 64-bit servers (HP Moonshot) finally arrived, BadUSB revealed hardware trust issues, Debian chose systemd, Chromebooks exceeded expectations with 35% notebook sales, and Btrfs saw wider adoption despite ongoing stability concerns.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627230/][Monkeysign 2.0]]: OpenPGP key-signing tool using QR codes instead of hex fingerprints to reduce user error; version 2.0 adds QR import from image files and was included in Debian Jessie.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627600/][Live kernel patching on track for 3.20]]: Live patching core functionality (abstracted from kPatch and kGraft) has been reviewed and agreed upon by both teams, ready for 3.20 kernel merge window.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627232/][CoreOS looks to move from Btrfs to overlayfs]]: CoreOS planning switch from Btrfs to ext4+overlayfs due to Btrfs issues with out-of-space errors, metadata rebalancing, and slow performance for Docker workloads.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627419/][The "too small to fail" memory-allocation rule]]: Kernel has unwritten rule that small GFP_KERNEL allocations (<=8 pages) never fail, which can cause OOM killer deadlocks when processes holding locks need memory to exit.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/627357/][Best of open hardware in 2014 (Opensource.com)]]: Opensource.com year-in-review covering open hardware developments including Arduino, Raspberry Pi, and related projects that advanced the open hardware ecosystem in 2014.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626426/][CollabMark and standardizing trademark policies for open projects]]: Stanford Law School's CIS launched CollabMark to create standardized trademark usage guidelines for open-source projects, releasing a boilerplate policy that projects can adopt.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626103/][Presenting with Sozi 14]]: Sozi presentation software evolved from an Inkscape extension to a standalone application, offering an alternative to LibreOffice Impress with its own distinct user experience.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/625969/][Kernel test automation with LTP]]: The Linux Test Project provides automated testing for the Linux kernel, reducing manual regression testing and helping catch bugs before release.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626559/][Plug-and-play sanitization of USB thumb drives]]: CIRCLean is a Debian-based Raspberry Pi project that automatically scans and sanitizes untrusted USB drives by converting suspicious files to safe formats before opening.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626294/][Scalability Techniques for Practical Synchronization Primitives (ACM Queue)]]: Davidlohr Bueso covers kernel locking scalability techniques for large high-end servers, including proportional backoff, hybrid spinlocks, and adaptive spinning strategies that reduce lock contention while maintaining fairness and responsiveness in multi-core environments.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626544/][On the problem of maintainer abuse]]: Jonathan Corbet discusses the controversy around posting large patch sets during Linux kernel merge windows, where Thomas Gleixner criticized the practice as "maintainer abuse" as subsystem maintainers are busy integrating changes; Kevin Cernekee proposed a formal patch submission moratorium during merge windows.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626665/][User namespaces and setgroups()]]: Eric Biederman's patches address a security vulnerability where unprivileged user namespace creation allowed dropping groups via setgroups(); the fix adds a /proc/PID/setgroups control file allowing processes to disable setgroups() within their namespace until group-ID mapping is established.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626110/][Launching CollabMark Project to Hack Trademarks for Free Culture]]: Stanford Law School's CIS launched CollabMark to help open-source and free culture communities navigate trademark law, offering a Collaborative Mark Policy template that projects can adopt to protect their names and logos while remaining compatible with open licensing principles.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626552/][Harmer: Overview of Qt3D 2.0 – Part 1]]: Sean Harmer details KDAB's revival of Qt3D as a competitive 3D framework for Qt5, leveraging OpenGL as the foundation for Qt Quick 2 rendering and providing a modern API for 3D graphics within the Qt ecosystem.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/626660/][Securing the future of GnuPG]]: The GnuPG project sought donations to fund two full-time developers (120,000 Euro/year) as only one underpaid developer maintained the critical cryptographic software; the article discusses GnuPG versions (1.4, 2.0, 2.1), PKCS#11 smartcard support issues, and GNOME keyring conflicts with gpg-agent.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/625051/][Snowdrift.coop: Funding for free projects]]: Snowdrift.coop implements a many-to-many matching funding model where patrons donate one cent per ten patrons supporting a project, creating collective funding without direct appeals using the Snowdrift Dilemma game theory to encourage participation.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/625535/][BPG, a still-image format from video compression]]: Fabrice Bellard's BPG (Better Portable Graphics) uses HEVC video compression to outperform JPEG in quality and file size, supporting 8-14 bit channels, alpha transparency, and lossless mode, though patent encumbrance makes it problematic for free software adoption.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624623/][A quick look at the new FontForge release]]: FontForge's 20141126 release adds multi-glyph display in editing windows, a local Node.js web server for live preview, stabilized Mac/Windows builds, and full UFO v3 support for font collaboration and interoperability with proprietary tools.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/625224/][Attaching eBPF programs to sockets]]: Linux 3.19 introduced SO_ATTACH_BPF for attaching eBPF programs to sockets, enabling per-packet processing with access to packet data and eBPF map statistics; programs can be written in raw BPF instruction format or a restricted C language compiled via LLVM.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/625077/][The iov_iter interface]]: Describes the iov_iter kernel primitive (added in 2.6.24 by Nick Piggin) for safely iterating through user-space buffer fragments via struct iov_iter containing type, offset, count, iov, and nr_segs fields; functions like copy_to_iter() and copy_from_iter() advance the iterator through buffers; expansion in 3.19 adds kvec support and formalizes the API for networking subsystem use.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/625578/][Linux Mint 17.1 review—less change is good change (Ars Technica)]]: Ars Technica reviews Linux Mint 17.1 (based on Ubuntu 14.04 LTS, supported until 2019), praising its focus on Cinnamon and MATE desktops while leveraging the stable LTS base; developers can ignore base system changes and focus on what makes Mint distinctive.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/625072/][Emacs and changing documentation formats]]: Eric S. Raymond proposed replacing Emacs's Texinfo documentation with AsciiDoc, arguing Texinfo is archaic and creates barriers to contribution; while some favored Org mode as an alternative, Richard Stallman indicated Org format could be acceptable if it generates quality output for PS, PDF, HTML, and plain text formats.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624600/][A new set of Docker tools]]: Docker announced three new container management tools: Machine for system provisioning, Swarm for native container clustering with a pluggable scheduler architecture and battery-included default, and Compose for assembling multi-container applications; the public API allows swapping schedulers while maintaining application portability.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624776/][Hutterer: pointer acceleration in libinput - building a DPI database for mice]]: Peter Hutterer describes libinput 0.7's new mechanism using physical mouse DPI resolution (from a udev hwdb database as of systemd 218) to provide consistent pointer acceleration across different mice; the MOUSE_DPI property is read by libinput and used as a reference point for acceleration calculations, with developers seeking contributions to populate the database.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624146/][The GnuPG 2.1 release]]: GnuPG 2.1.0 marks the first official release of the "modern" series, introducing libsecret integration for key storage, elliptic curve cryptography support, and parallel agent operations; the version cannot be installed alongside the 2.0 series and lacks extensive real-world testing despite being labeled as stable.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/622404/][McKenney: Stupid RCU Tricks: rcutorture Catches an RCU Bug]]: Paul McKenney details how rcutorture testing caught an RCU bug requiring approximately 200-300 hours to reproduce due to its sparse failure rate; better random number generation in testing enabled faster bisection and identification of the culprit.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/622644/][Version 2 of the kdbus patches posted]]: Second version of kernel-level D-Bus replacement introduces a filesystem-based interface (kdbusfs) replacing the /dev/kdbus device approach; kdbus implements the D-Bus protocol in the kernel to enable features impossible in userspace while maintaining protocol compatibility.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624126/][ACCESS_ONCE() and compiler bugs]]: GCC 4.6 and 4.7 drop volatile semantics for non-scalar types passed to ACCESS_ONCE(), causing silent kernel bugs when used with types like pte_t; the kernel's policy is to blacklist buggy compiler versions rather than add workarounds.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624258/][Splicing out syscalls for tiny kernels]]: Developers propose removing splice(), sendfile(), and tee() syscalls to save 8KB on memory-constrained embedded systems; debate centers on whether removing syscalls creates a dangerous precedent, with advocates arguing embedded developers should control their system call set.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624045/][Version 2 of the kdbus patch set]]: The second version of kdbus replaces device files with a virtual filesystem (kdbusfs) mounted at /sys/fs/kdbus, addresses metadata security concerns by letting senders control what information accompanies messages, and adds a 64-bit unique process identifier to prevent PID reuse race conditions.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/620827/][Some 3.18 development statistics]]: Linux 3.18 development accumulated 11,186 non-merge changesets from 1,428 developers with Intel and Red Hat as leading employers; approximately 11% of contributions came from volunteers while 1,521 first-time developers entered the kernel community during this cycle.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624379/][BSP in Switzerland (St-Cergue)]]: A Debian Bug Squashing Party scheduled for January 30 to February 1, 2015 in St-Cergue, Switzerland aims to bring together Debian contributors to address bugs for the Jessie release and Stretch development cycle.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624381/][They make Mageia: David Walser (Mageia Blog)]]: David Walser began contributing to Mageia after discovering a security update version import issue where Mandriva's release version was imported rather than the updates version, prompting him to file bugs for missing security updates and assist the QA team.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624349/][The Rocket containerization system]]: CoreOS launched Rocket as a lightweight container alternative to Docker, emphasizing composable independent tools, image auditing, and application identity through a standardized App Container Image (ACI) specification.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/623349/][Kawa — fast scripting on the Java platform]]: Kawa is a Scheme-based language for the JVM that combines dynamic scripting with compiled language performance, supporting nearly all of the R7RS specification. Its optional type annotations enable compiler optimization, and expressions in the REPL are compiled on-the-fly to JVM bytecode, providing fast startup compared to other JVM scripting languages. Used in projects including MIT App Inventor and Nü Echo.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624391/][QEMU Advent Calendar 2014 unveiled]]: The QEMU project launched an Advent Calendar site at qemu-advent-calendar.org, offering daily downloadable virtual machine disk images for QEMU exploration starting December 1, 2014, with an initial Slackware image.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/623875/][Rocket, a new container runtime from CoreOS]]: CoreOS announced Rocket as a lightweight Docker alternative, criticizing Docker's expansion into cloud server provisioning, clustering, and other functions beyond a simple container runtime. Rocket emphasizes composable tools, image auditing, and application identity through the App Container Image (ACI) specification.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/622682/][Introducing AcousticBrainz]]: AcousticBrainz is a crowd-sourced MusicBrainz project cataloging audio features like tempo, genre, mood, key, and scale using the open-source Essentia toolkit from Universitat Pompeu Fabra, complementing the existing AcoustID fingerprinting database.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624028/][New features in Git 2.2.0]]: Git 2.2.0 introduces signed pushes via the --signed flag, which applies GPG signatures to push certificates sent during git push; receive-pack can verify these certificates and log successful verifications for audit trails, helping prevent man-in-the-middle attacks.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/623213/][Mapping the world with open source (Opensource.com)]]: An interview with Paul Ramsey of Boundless (self-described "Red Hat of geospatial") discussing open source GIS tools including PostGIS (spatial SQL database), GeoServer (web map publishing), OpenLayers (browser-based mapping), and QGIS (desktop GIS), with a focus on "Spatial IT" — making spatial data accessible across enterprise workflows beyond specialized GIS departments.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624140/][The Impact of the Linux Philosophy (Opensource.com)]]: An Opensource.com article examining how Linux's philosophy of user control and flexibility distinguishes it from other operating systems, illustrated with a "nail gun" analogy: Linux lets users pull the trigger as they choose, while other OSes restrict what you can do even for routine tasks.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/624340/][JavaScript for Kids -- New from No Starch Press]]: Announcement of "JavaScript for Kids" by Nick Morgan (Twitter frontend engineer), a playful introduction covering JavaScript basics (strings, arrays, loops), progressing to jQuery and Canvas graphics, with fun examples like bouncing balls and complete games like Snake plus end-of-chapter programming challenges.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/621682/][Fuzz and strings]]: Michał Zalewski discovered that the `strings` utility from GNU binutils can cause code execution when scanning untrusted binaries due to range-checking bugs in libbfd's object-file parser. Many distributions lack ASLR, making exploitation easier; using `strings -a` (simple byte-by-byte scan) avoids the vulnerable libbfd code path.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/621046/][Introducing lazytime]]: A new `lazytime` mount option for ext4 (proposed by Ted Ts'o) keeps atime current in memory but only writes the inode to disk when another change occurs, satisfying POSIX requirements without the performance cost of constant atime updates. Dave Chinner suggested implementing it in the VFS layer to benefit all filesystems.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/621006/][Control group namespaces]]: Containers use cgroups and namespaces for OS-level isolation, but cgroups themselves aren't virtualized, allowing container processes to see the global cgroup hierarchy. A new cgroup namespace (CLONE_NEWCGROUP flag for unshare()) solves this by providing a private view of the cgroup tree, addressing information leakage and enabling container migration via CRIU.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/621612/][The trouble with dropping groups]]: Allowing unprivileged processes to drop group memberships (proposed for sandboxing) faces a hidden obstacle: some systems like Tizen use groups for negative access control, where ACLs deny access to resources when the process is a member of specific groups. This mechanism would break if processes could discard groups at will.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/621526/][Live kernel patching for SUSE Enterprise Linux]]: SUSE is now using kGraft for live kernel patching in its enterprise distribution, which doesn't require stopping the whole system during patching. Unlike some alternatives, it's fully open source and SUSE is working with upstream to ensure sustainable kernel live patching on Linux.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/620487/][The Long and Winding Road (Mageia Blog)]]: Mageia 5 Beta 1 was delayed due to RPM 4.12 upgrade issues during the release process, causing important metadata problems that required a second mass rebuild in October before Beta 1 ISOs could be delivered for QA testing.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/621156/][Linux for lettuce (Opensource.com)]]: Covers the Open Source Seed Initiative (OSSI) applying open source concepts to plant breeding to protect seeds as a commons. Inspired by open source software, OSSI uses intellectual property tools to create and enforce sharing in plant genetic resources, countering increasingly patent-encumbered seed ownership.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/621787/][Lauren Ipsum: A Story About Computer Science and Other Improbable Things]]: A children's book by Carlos Bueno (No Starch Press, Dec 2014) that teaches computational thinking through a fantasy adventure following young protagonist Lauren as she encounters programming concepts and puzzles in a land running on logic, aimed at kids and those wanting an accessible introduction to computer science fundamentals.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619992/][The Grumpy Editor's guide to surviving the systemd debate]]: Jonathan Corbet's editorial argues that the heated systemd debate has inflated importance beyond its significance as just an init system, pointing to past disputes like devfs that resolved without community destruction; suggests all parties assume good faith, systemd critics explore alternatives like Gentoo/Slackware rather than siege mentality, and the community will eventually reach equilibrium whether systemd succeeds or gets replaced.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619784/][High-DPI displays and Linux]]: Tests ThinkPad X1 Carbon's 2560x1440 display reveal Linux still struggles with high-DPI screens; GNOME/KDE use pixel scaling (easy but blurry) or DPI-aware rendering (better but requires app cooperation); external monitors break when scaled for high-DPI; Wayland promises improvement but fractional scaling still problematic; suggests real solution requires divorcing apps from pixels entirely.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619376/][The security state of KVM]]: Paolo Bonzini summarizes Google security team's analysis of KVM hypervisor attack surface; team found 9 vulnerabilities (mostly race conditions and buffer overflows in device emulation); many bugs found in ASSERT() macros compiled out in production; goal is moving emulation to userspace to reduce attack surface by 50% with <0.1% performance impact; ~40k lines of emulated x86 instructions are the main concern.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619514/][An introduction to compound pages]]: Linux kernel uses compound pages (contiguous page groups) primarily for huge pages in hugetlbfs and transparent huge pages; created with __GFP_COMP flag, differs from simple higher-order allocation; head page marked PG_head, tail pages PG_tail; metadata (order, destructor) stored in second tail page's struct page fields; tail pages have pointer to head via compound_head(); anonymous memory and kernel buffers can use compound pages but not page cache.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618411/][A control group manager]]: CGManager is a daemon for managing cgroups, developed for LXC containers but originally designed as an alternative to systemd's cgroup management for non-systemd distributions; uses D-Bus for requests, supports unprivileged nested containers, avoids delegating cgroupfs to unprivileged processes;Serge Hallyn presented at LinuxCon Europe 2014.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618888/][Smartcard features on the YubiKey NEO]]: YubiKey NEO smartcard functionality matured since April 2014, now supports multiple OATH-TOTP/HOTP credentials via JavaCard applet (removing the 2-slot limit), OpenPGP applet with RSA 2048/EC, PIV applet for FIPS compliance, and U2F support on newer models; desktop Python and Android apps configure and display TOTP codes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619066/][Vetter: Atomic Modeset Support for KMS Drivers]]: Daniel Vetter posted atomic modeset helper library series to ease transition for existing KMS graphics drivers to atomic modesetting; existing helper libraries and driver callbacks don't fit new semantics requiring restructuring; covers changes needed for atomic modeset support using new helper libraries.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619058/][Supporting solid-state hybrid drives]]: Kernel patch set proposes using I/O priority bits to communicate cache advice to hybrid drives (IOPRIO_ADV_WILLNEED/DONTNEED/EVICT); criticized for per-process rather than per-file policy; alternative class-based approach (transaction/streaming/metadata/paging/data/background) suggested for better flexibility across drives, NFS, and persistent memory.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619146/][open() flags: O_TMPFILE and O_BENEATH]]: O_TMPFILE creates invisible temporary files without directory entries (bug fixed: mode argument now applied correctly); O_BENEATH flag for openat() constrains paths to prevent symlink escapes, developed for Capsicum seccomp sandboxing; both improve file creation security and temporary file handling in kernel.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619158/][Chromium and distributions]]: Paweł Hajdan Jr. (Google) presented at LinuxCon Europe 2014 on improving Chromium/Linux relations since 2009; ~150 open-source packages in Chromium; bundled libraries in third_party visible due to cross-platform needs; 17 libraries unbundled including bzip2, HarfBuzz, ICU, Speex; still uses forks of hunspell, Mesa, SQLite; packager patches now merged within hours; distributions like Gentoo/Arch help test with newer libraries.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619173/][Happy birthday FreeBSD]]: FreeBSD 1.0 released November 1, 1993; brief announcement noting the 21st birthday of the BSD-derived operating system.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619160/][A look at Pitivi 0.94]]: Pitivi video editor 0.94 released after crowdfunding campaign; UI improvements including GtkHeaderBar, undocked component position memory, title editor redesign; major under-the-hood changes: port to Python 3, rewrite of video viewer to use GStreamer OpenGL sink instead of Clutter, removal of CoGL library; planned replacement of GNonLin with new NLE library to fix deadlocks/freeszes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/619103/][Introducing Dynomite - Making non-distributed databases, distributed]]: Netflix open-sourced Dynomite, a database distribution system that turns single-server datastores into peer-to-peer linearly scalable clustered systems while preserving native client/server protocols (e.g., Redis); available under Apache license.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618682/][KVM Matures, and the Use Cases Multiply (Linux.com)]]: Adam Jollans reports from KVM Forum 2014 on KVM's OpenStack integration, NFV applications, and new white paper; panel discussed latency/throughput/jitter requirements for network function virtualization on general purpose hardware and fast VM communication approaches.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618422/][A look at Emacs 24.4]]: Emacs 24.4 adds electric indentation default, superword-mode for code, eww built-in web browser, text-mode menu support, and improved security with package signature verification and ACL support; introduces rectangle-mark-mode and frame layout save/restore.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618282/][The Google Summer of Code Reunion]]: GSoC 10th anniversary reunion featured Torvalds and Dirk Hohndel as Subsurface mentors; discussions covered paid vs unpaid FLOSS contributors and making projects more approachable to new contributors through mentoring programs and easy-hack initiatives.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618184/][Darkcoin: A cryptocurrency with more anonymity]]: Darkcoin uses DarkSend mixing via masternodes (requires 1000 DRK stake) to obscure transactions through pooled mixing; achieves anonymity through multiple rounds but security researcher notes masternodes can record input-output relationships; merchants accept DRK but Tor-hidden black markets also use it.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617842/][Garrett: Linux Container Security]]: Matthew Garrett argues containers have larger attack surface than hypervisors and need work on auditing, fuzzing, nested LSM support, and introspection; notes modern deployment uses kernel security features but companies selling container services haven't contributed meaningfully to improving them.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618074/][Toward better CPU idle-time predictions]]: Daniel Lezcano's cpuidle improvements integrate scheduler with idle subsystem using next timer expiration and latency requirements; tracks I/O completion times in 200µs buckets moved to front after 5 hits for better predictions; future version likely uses block layer device data instead of per-task tracking.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618421/][In a bind with binder]]: The Android IPC binder mechanism, proposed for movement from kernel staging to mainline, sparked debate; Greg Kroah-Hartman cited ABI stability needs while developers raised concerns about maintenance, security audit requirements, and whether moving "horrible" code encourages poor Android integration practices.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618333/][A desktop kernel wishlist]]: GNOME developer Bastien Nocera's kernel wishlist covering power management (hybrid suspend, connected standby, wake event reporting) and filesystem improvements (better inotify/fanotify, recursive directory timestamp updates) sparked discussion on implementing friendlier kernel APIs for desktop environments.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618152/][A look at the Crosswalk web runtime]]: Crosswalk is an HTML5 web runtime for Tizen and Android built on Blink/Chromium, supporting newer web standards than the old WebKit-based runtime; provides cross-platform web app framework with features like Web Components, Service Workers, raw sockets, and Native Client for native-like performance.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617833/][Schaller: GStreamer Conference 2014 talks online]]: Christian Schaller announced that videos from the GStreamer Conference 2014 are now available online through Ubicast, offering access to recorded talks shortly after the conference concluded.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617988/][Taiga, a new open source project management tool with focus on usability (Opensource.com)]]: Taiga is an open-source agile project management tool created by Kaleidos, featuring virtual sprint boards and poker-style story point estimation; designed to address shortcomings of existing tools like Redmine and Trac for agile planning workflows.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/618193/][Season of KDE 2014]]: Season of KDE is a community outreach program similar to Google Summer of Code, managed by the same KDE team; offers students and newcomers an alternative path to contributing to KDE through mentored projects with a November 5 mentor deadline.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617594/][Accessibility and the graphics stack]]: XDC 2014 talk by Samuel Thibault covering accessibility challenges in X and Wayland, from color blindness to motor control issues; discusses input methods (sticky keys, virtual keyboards, braille devices) and output requirements for screen readers using ATK, with concerns about Wayland maintaining accessibility parity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617555/][Tizen developers contemplate the Internet of Things]]: TDS 2014 presentations on IoT strategies for Tizen, including OIC (Open Interconnect Consortium) protocol stack and Tizen Micro, a stripped-down Yocto-based profile for headless devices running on Intel Galileo and MinnowBoard MAX.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617529/][Metrics for free-software communities]]: Fossetcon talk by Liferay's James Falkner on distinguishing vanity metrics from useful ones, using Bitergia tools (GPL-licensed Python project) to track contributions across forums, mailing lists, and code repositories; warns that measuring wrong things creates perverse incentives like farming rat tails.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617370/][Where to store your encrypted data]]: LinuxCon Europe talk by Kolab Systems CEO Georg Greve on encrypted data storage decisions covering legal frameworks (US vs Swiss jurisdiction), physical security (own hardware in caged data centers), and software tradeoffs (open-source trust, browser security); service MyKolab.com runs on Swiss-hosted Kolab software with favorable privacy laws.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/616859/][Device tree overlays]]: Pantelis Antoniou presented device tree overlay infrastructure merged in Linux 3.17-3.18, enabling dynamic device tree modification via changesets (of_changeset_apply/revert) and phandle resolution for fragments, solving hardware description for BeagleBone capes, FPGA-based systems, and other dynamically-configured devices.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617383/][Three talks on kernel development tools]]: Three kernel development tools presented at LPC - Coccinelle for backporting ~800 drivers to older kernels by automating #ifdef migration, undertaker-checkpatch for detecting dead/undead #ifdef blocks (found 600+ in 3.17), and Vampyr for generating maximizing set of kernel configs to test patches.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617140/][The future of the realtime patch set]]: Thomas Gleixner announced the realtime Linux patch set has moved to hobby status due to lack of industry funding; despite contributing high-res timers, tickless patches, threaded IRQs, and lockdep to mainline, the project faces widening gap from upstream changes.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617543/][Tizen Common and open hardware]]: Leon Anavi and Philippe Coval discussed running Tizen Common base profile on open-source SBCs - tizen-sunxi for Allwinner A10/A20 boards and direct boot on MinnowBoard MAX (Intel Atom), enabling dual-boot with Android on some devices.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617527/][What's New in Android 5.0 Lollipop (Android Developers Blog)]]: Android 5.0 Lollipop introduced Material Design visual language, improved performance, and expanded across phones, tablets, wearables, TVs, and cars as the largest Android update to date.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/616901/][The Debian init system general resolution returns]]: The Debian Technical Committee resolved the init system debate using the chairman's casting vote as specified in the Debian Constitution. Technical analysis favored systemd while Upstart supporters were largely Canonical contributors with vested interests. Ian Jackson challenged the process with procedural motions including a motion to depose the TC chairman.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617355/][On the sickness of our community]]: Commentary distinguishing useful moderation (including post removal when necessary) from destructive behavior like replacing posts with "fart fart fart". The author argues there's a meaningful difference between appropriate moderation and being an asshole.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617256/][Thomas Gleixner at the 2014 Linux Plumbers Conference]]: Photo coverage of Thomas Gleixner's appearance at LPC 2014, showing him presenting at the conference.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617341/][Interview: Thomas Voß of Mir (Linux Voice)]]: Interview discussing the Mir display server project and the frustration of individual contributors when pressured by groups, noting that applying pressure on people is not the same as forcing them to act.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/616743/][Interview: Thomas Voß of Mir (Linux Voice)]]: Canonical's Thomas Voß explains Mir's decision to standardize on an API (like Android and Wayland) rather than define a protocol, supporting EGL and GL as the single open graphics language for app and toolkit developers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617517/][New from Pragmatic Bookshelf: "Programming Elixir"]]: Elixir is a functional, concurrent language built on the Erlang VM with pragmatic syntax and metaprogramming support, designed for experienced programmers exploring functional programming and concurrent applications.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/617514/][Android Security Internals - New from No Starch Press]]: Nikolay Elenkov's book covers Android security architecture from the ground up, explaining Binder IPC, permissions system, cryptographic providers, and device administration for security professionals and Android developers.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/616097/][Graphics drivers and the BSDs]]: Representatives from FreeBSD, DragonFly BSD, and OpenBSD discussed the state of DRM graphics drivers for their systems at XDC, following the 2008 split when DRM moved into the Linux kernel tree.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/615906/][WikiHouse: Open-source architecture]]: WikiHouse is an open-source construction system allowing anyone to design, download, and CNC-mill houses with minimal skill for under £50k, using Creative Commons Zero Public Domain Dedication.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/616272/][Toybox reaches version 0.5]]: Rob Landley's minimalist Linux CLI utility suite (BusyBox replacement) released version 0.5 under BSD license, implementing grep, tar, mount, and other core commands in a single executable for embedded systems with support for both fully stable and pending commands.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/615716/][CUPS reaches version 2.0]]: CUPS 2.0 released with IPP Everywhere support for mobile devices, GnuTLS replacement of OpenSSL enabling X.509 certificate validation, systemd integration for Linux, and security improvements including PAM-based authentication and job-history DoS throttling (default limit 500).
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/616330/][OpenH264 Now in Firefox]]: Firefox integrated Cisco's open-source H.264 decoder into WebRTC to improve interoperability with existing telecommunication infrastructure, since VP8 failed to gain sufficient adoption despite Mozilla's advocacy for royalty-free codecs.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/615994/][The Linux Foundation announces Dronecode]]: Dronecode project supports APM autopilot and ArduPilot/PX4 open hardware platforms for autonomous drones, with over 1200 developers contributing and Linux-based boards emerging as a new target for hobby-level vehicles.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/616223/][White paper: the state of KVM]]: Linux Foundation white paper covers KVM's trajectory with OpenStack as the primary growth driver, noting KVM's position as the most popular hypervisor for OpenStack deployments.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/613392/][The bug parade meets the zombies]]: Gary McGraw's AppSec keynote emphasized that half of security issues are design flaws not bugs, criticized C/C++ for buffer overflows, highlighted race conditions as increasingly critical for multi-core systems, and recommended IEEE's "Avoiding the Top 10 Security Flaws" and BSIMM framework for measuring security maturity.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/613284/][Google and Adobe's pan-CJK open font]]: Google and Adobe created Noto Sans CJK/Source Han Sans, the largest open-source font project with ~500,000 characters across Chinese, Japanese, and Korean scripts. The project maxed out OpenType's 65,535 glyph limit per file and required donated CFF rendering engine to FreeType, overcoming Han unification and encoding standard challenges. Released July 2014 in seven weights under Apache 2 license.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/614218/][Bash gets shellshocked]]: The Shellshock vulnerability (discovered Sept 24, 2014) allowed remote code execution through environment variable parsing, existing in Bash since ~1992. Attack vectors included CGI, DHCP clients, mail servers, and restricted SSH logins. Initial patches were fragile; the final fix used namespace isolation with prefix/suffix on function names. Distributions using dash for /bin/sh were less vulnerable.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/614349/][Top ten web attack techniques of 2013]]: WhiteHat Security's 2014 AppSec USA presentation ranked community-voted web hacking techniques, with #1 being Mutation XSS using JavaScript innerHTML mutation. The list highlights evolving web attack patterns and defense considerations.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/614348/][Foo over UDP]]: Tom Herbert's FOU (Foo over UDP) patch set for Linux 3.18 implements UDP-level tunneling for IP encapsulation protocols, leveraging existing UDP hardware support to enable efficient UDP-based IP tunneling.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/614057/][How implementation details become ABI: a case study]]: A renameat2() change in Linux 3.15 caused unintended behavior when renaming files with short names (< DNAME_INLINE_LEN), affecting /proc/self/fd/X symlink behavior. This demonstrates how internal kernel implementation details can inadvertently become stable ABI constraints.
- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/615809/][Implementing virtual system calls]]: The vDSO is a kernel-exported shared library that allows read-only system calls like gettimeofday() to execute in user space, avoiding costly context switches. On x86_64, four virtual system calls (__vdso_clock_gettime, __vdso_gettimeofday, __vdso_time, __vdso_getcpu) are provided via the vsyscall page, achieving ~4x speedup (22μs vs 90μs for gettimeofday). Implementation relies on clever linker script additions to map kernel data into user space.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/614140/][Android apps on the desktop]]: Google's App Runtime for Chrome (ARC) enables Android apps to run on Chrome OS via a Chrome extension using Native Client (NaCl) sandboxing and Dalvik VM. Developer Vlad Filippov created ARChon, a custom rebuild allowing Android apps to run on other Linux desktop systems by repackaging apps into Chrome web-app templates with updated manifest.json files. Many apps fail due to reliance on proprietary Google Play Services library, which remains unavailable on non-Chrome platforms.

- [[https://lwn.net/Articles/614358/][Sync things with Syncthing]]: Syncthing is an MIT-licensed peer-to-peer file synchronization system written in Go that keeps directories synchronized across arbitrary nodes using TLS 1.2 with perfect forward secrecy. Nodes discover each other via SSDP or global discovery server, with each machine having a unique RSA key and SSL certificate fingerprint as its node ID. Unlike cloud-based solutions, all data transfers directly between peers without going through a central server.
